Evidence Required for Inheritance Division: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on evidence requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the requirement of evidence for dividing inherited real estate, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each position.

Core Idea
Evidence is required to divide inherited real estate according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn allow division based on the heirs' admission alone.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: can a judge divide inherited real estate when the heirs are in possession but produce no formal evidence? Abu Hanifa insists on witnesses; the Sahibayn trust the heirs' word. Let's explore their proofs and the practical difference in legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the exact point of disagreement: the condition for permissibility of dividing inherited real estate by a judge when claimants are in possession but lack external evidence.
The property is real estate (house or land), not movable.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa requires witnesses to prove the death of the deceased and that the claimants are the sole heirs. His proofs: real estate is durable so delay is harmless; division is a judgment against the deceased requiring certainty.
He prioritizes certainty to avoid overturning judgments if omitted heirs appear.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani allow division based solely on the claimants' admission (i'tiraf). Their proof: Muslims are just (based on Umar's letter to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari) and if an heir appears later, the division can be revisited.
They prioritize trust and practicality.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, heirs must bring witnesses; under the Sahibayn, they only need to claim and possess. This affects the ease and speed of property division.
The risk of omitted heirs is handled differently: Abu Hanifa prevents it, Sahibayn cures it later.
5
Note the tarjih in later practice
Although the passage does not state a preferred view, later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn for feasibility. Understand that both positions are valid within the school.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf among equals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حضر الشركاء عند القاضى وفى ايديهم دار وضيعة وادعوا انهم ورثوها عن فلان لم يقسمها القاضي عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى حتى يقيموا البينة على موته وعدد ورثته وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى يُقسمها باعترافهم . كچھ لوگ قاضی کے پاس آکر یوں کہے کہ یہ زمین ہے یا یہ گھر ہے یہ فلاں آدمی کا تھا، اب وہ مرگیا ہے اور ہم لوگ اس کے وارث ہیں ۔ اس کو ہمارے درمیان تقسیم کر دیں تو امام ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کے لئے اس وقت تک تقسیم کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے جب تک کہ فلاں آدمی کے مرنے پر گواہ قائم نہ کریں۔ اور اس بات پر بھی گواہ قائم کریں کہ ہم ہی لوگ وارث ہیں ہمارے علاوہ اور کوئی وارث نہیں ۔ ان دونوں باتوں پر گواہ قائم کرے تب ان کے درمیان گھر یاز میں تقسیم کر دے۔ زمین خود محفوظ ہے، زمانہ دراز کے بعد بھی اس میں کوئی زیادہ خامی نہیں آتی اور یہی حال گھر کا ہے۔ اس لئے سال چھ مہینے تاخیر کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بینہ قائم کروا کر پوری تحقیق کر لینی چاہئے (۲) جب تک مال تقسیم نہیں ہوا ہے تو یہ میت کا مال شمار کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے تقسیم کرنا گویا کہ میت کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنا ہے۔ اور کسی کے خلاف فیصلہ کرنے کے لئے گواہ چاہئے ۔ اس لئے بھی گواہ قائم کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ یہ بات بھی واضح ہو جائے کہ فلان مر چکا ہے اور یہ بھی کہ ان کے علاوہ وارث نہیں ہے۔ ورنہ ابھی تقسیم کر دیں اور بعد میں کوئی وارث ظاہر ہو جائے تو قضا توڑنا پڑے گا اس لئے گواہ قائم کرے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ تقسیم کر دے۔ کیونکہ مسلمان ظاہری طور پر عادل ہیں۔ اثر میں ہے۔ کتب عمر بن الخطاب الى ابى موسى الاشعرى ... المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض (الف) (دارقطنی ، باب کتاب عمر الی موسی الاشعری ، ج رابع ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۴۴۲۵ ) جب مسلمان ظاہری طور پر عادل ہیں اور ان کے خلاف کوئی قرینہ نہیں ہے اس لئے جب وہ کہتے ہیں کہ تقسیم کر دیں تو تقسیم کر سکتے ہیں۔ اور بعد میں وارث ظاہر ہوئے تو دوبارہ صحیح تقسیم کر دی جائے گی (۲) جیسے منقولی جائداد کو بغیر بعینہ قائم کئے تقسیم کر دیتے ہیں۔
When the partners come before the judge and in their possession is a house or land and they claim that they inherited it from so-and-so, the judge does not divide it according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) until they produce evidence of his death and the number of his heirs. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said (may Allah have mercy on them): He divides it based on their admission. Some people come to the judge and say: This land or this house belonged to so-and-so, now he has died and we are his heirs. Divide it among us. Imam Abu Hanifa says: It is not correct for the judge to divide until they produce witnesses on the death of that person and also produce witnesses that they are the heirs and there is no other heir besides them. After producing witnesses on both matters, then he divides the house or land among them. Land is durable, even after a long time it does not deteriorate much, and the same is true for a house. Therefore, there is no harm in delaying for a year or six months. So he should have evidence established and conduct full investigation. (2) As long as the property is not divided, it is considered the property of the deceased, so dividing it is like making a judgment against the deceased. And for making a judgment against someone, witnesses are required. Therefore, it is necessary to have witnesses established so that it becomes clear that so-and-so has died and that there are no other heirs besides them. Otherwise, if they divide now and later another heir appears, the judgment would have to be overturned. So he should have witnesses established. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: Let him divide, because Muslims are apparently just. There is an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Muslims are reliable witnesses for each other.' (Darqutni) When Muslims are apparently just and there is no contrary evidence against them, then when they say 'divide,' he can divide. And if later an heir appears, the correct division will be repeated. (2) Just as movable property is divided without establishing evidence.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of inherited real estate (house or land) when the claimants are in possession but lack formal evidence. The text first states the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the judge must not divide the property until the claimants produce witnesses (bayyinah) to prove two facts: (a) the death of the deceased from whom they inherited, and (b) the number of heirs (i.e., that they are the only heirs). The reasoning is twofold: (1) real estate is durable, so delay causes no harm; (2) division of property before it is distributed is effectively a judgment against the deceased, which requires proof. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree: the judge may divide based solely on the claimants' admission (i'tiraf), because Muslims are presumed just (a principle derived from the letter of Umar to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari). If an omitted heir appears later, the division can be revisited. The text thus presents both views with their respective rationales.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, specifically testimony of witnesses in a legal context.
الشركاء (al-shurakā'): The partners, here referring to the heirs who jointly own the property.
ورثوها (warithūhā): They inherited it (feminine singular object). Past tense verb.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners.
اعتراف (i‘tirāf): Admission or confession, here the heirs' own statement that they are heirs.
عدول (‘udūl): Plural of ‘adl, meaning just and reliable witnesses/people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what is the basis for allowing the judge to divide inherited real estate without formal evidence?
A) Real estate is durable and delay is harmless.
B) Division is a judgment against the deceased requiring certainty.
C) Muslims are presumed just, so their admission suffices.
D) The judge must always trust claimants in possession.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on evidence for inheritance division: Abu Hanifa insists on formal proof to avoid harm, while the Sahibayn trust the heirs' word for practicality; later practice often adopts the latter view.

Division Based on Heirs' Admission
A record that division is done based on heirs' admission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of inherited property based on heirs' admission and identify the supporting authority in the judge's record.

Core Idea
Division of inherited property may be based on the heirs' own admission without requiring external witnesses.

This short passage from the Book of Division (Kitab al-Qismah) records an important practice: the judge divides the estate based on the heirs' own statement that their predecessor died and they are his heirs. This note confirms the validity of such a division within the Hanafi school, supporting the view of the Sahibayn over a stricter requirement for witnesses. Understanding this nuance clarifies the evidentiary standards for inheritance division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basis
Recognize that the act being described is the division of inherited property, and the basis for division is the heirs' own statement (admission).
The phrase 'bi-qawlihim' (based on their statement) is key.
2
Identify the authority source
Note that this practice is recorded in the judge's official book (Kitab al-Qadi), which lends it authority within the madhhab.
This is a record of practice, not a direct fatwa.
3
Understand the intra-madhhab context
Recognize that this record supports the Sahibayn view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that admission suffices, as opposed to Abu Hanifa who required witnesses.
The passage does not mention the dispute but implies a preference.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a case where three children come to a judge and state they are the only heirs. According to this record, the judge can divide the estate based on their admission alone.
The admission must be clear and free from coercion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذكر في كتاب القسمة انها قسمها بقولهم . كتاب القاضی میں یہ مسئلہ لکھا ہوا ہے کہ اگر وارثین خود اقرار کریں کہ ہمارا مورث مر گیا ہے اور ہم لوگ اس کے وارث ہیں تو ان کے اقرار کی وجہ سے زمین اور گھر بھی تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔
And it is mentioned in the Book of Division that he divided it based on their statement. In the Book of the Judge (Kitab al-Qadi) it is written that if the heirs themselves admit that our predecessor has died and we are his heirs, then due to their admission, the land and house will also be divided.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This short passage supplements the previous dispute by noting that in the judge's official record (Kitab al-Qisma or Kitab al-Qadi), the division is recorded as having been performed based on the heirs' own admission (qawl/qarar). This implies that the preferred practice even in the madhhab may be to rely on the Sahibayn's view, as the judge documents the admission as the basis.

Key Terms
كتاب القسمة (Kitāb al-Qismah): The chapter or book on division of property within fiqh works.
بقولهم (bi-qawlihim): Based on their statement / admission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is recorded in the Book of Division regarding division of inherited land when heirs admit their inheritance?
A) That division cannot be done until witnesses testify.
B) That division is done based on their admission.
C) That the property must be sold and proceeds divided.
D) That only the judge can decide without any input.

Key Takeaway
Division of inheritance can be validly based on the heirs' own admission without external witnesses, as recorded in the judge's book.

Division of Movable Property Without Evidence
Ruling on dividing movable inheritance property without evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing movable property claimed as inheritance without evidence and explain the rationale for immediate division.

Core Idea
Movable property claimed as inheritance is divided immediately without evidence because it is perishable.

In inheritance disputes, the need to preserve property sometimes overrides strict evidentiary requirements. This lesson explores a unique Hanafi ruling where all three founding imams agree: if the property in question is movable (manqūl) and the claimants assert it is inheritance, the judge should divide it promptly, even without witnesses to the death or heirship. The key reason is the perishable nature of movable goods, which could be lost or damaged if delayed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property type
Determine whether the property is real estate (ʿiqār) or movable (manqūl). The ruling applies only to movable property.
Movable property includes items like livestock, jewelry, cash, and furniture.
2
Assess the claimants' assertion
The claimants must assert that the property is inheritance from a deceased relative and that they are the heirs. No further evidence is required.
The claim alone is sufficient.
3
State the ruling
According to all Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani), the judge divides the property immediately among the claimants.
This is the muftā bihi position.
4
Explain the rationale
The reason is that movable property is subject to spoilage, loss, or theft. Quick division allows each heir to safeguard his share.
If an heir appears later, the division can be corrected.
5
Contrast with real estate
For real estate, the judge requires evidence of death and the number of heirs before dividing. This exception is due to the durability of land.
This contrast is important for understanding the scope of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان المال المشترك مما سوى العقار وادعوا انه ميراث قسمه فى قولهم جميعا . اور اگر مال مشترک زمین کے علاوہ ہوا اور وہ دعوی کریں کہ ان کی میراث ہے تو سب کے قول میں یہ ہے کہ اس کو تقسیم کر دے۔ شرق مشترک مال ہے اور زمین اور گھر کے علاوہ وہ مال ہے، ورثہ کہتے ہیں کہ وہ مال فلاں مورث سے ہم کو ملا ہے اور ہم لوگ اس کے وارث ہیں تو چاہے مورث کے مرنے پر اور وارث کی تعداد پر گواہ نہ پیش کریں پھر بھی امام ابو حنفیہ اور صاحبین متینوں امام یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کو تقسیم کردے۔ زمین اور گھر کے علاوہ جو منقولی جائداد ہے وہ جلدی میں خراب ہو سکتی ہے اس لئے اس کو جلدی تقسیم کر دے تا کہ ہر وارث اپنے اپنے حصے کی حفاظت کرتا رہے۔ اور بعد میں کوئی وارث ظاہر ہوگا تو دوبارہ صحیح تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔
If the joint property is other than real estate (movable) and they claim it is inheritance, it is divided according to the statement of all of them. And if the joint property is other than land (movable property) and they claim it is their inheritance, then according to all (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn), he divides it. Movable property is property other than land and house. Heirs say that the property came to us from so-and-so and we are his heirs; then even if they do not bring witnesses on the death of the predecessor or the number of heirs, Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, may Allah have mercy on them, all say that he should divide it. Movable property, other than land and house, can deteriorate quickly. Therefore, he should divide it quickly so that each heir can safeguard his own share. And if an heir appears later, the correct division will be made again.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling where all three founding imams of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree: if the property claimed as inheritance is movable (non-real estate), the judge should divide it immediately based solely on the claimants' assertion, without requiring evidence of death or number of heirs. The reason is that movable property is perishable—it may spoil, be lost, or diminish in value. Quick division allows each heir to preserve his share. If a missing heir emerges later, the division can be rectified. This is consistent with the Sahibayn's general view already mentioned; here Abu Hanifa concurs due to the risk of loss.

Key Terms
عقار (‘iqār): Real estate, immovable property (land, buildings).
مال مشترك (māl mushtarak): Jointly owned property held by co-owners.
منقول (manqūl): Movable property; anything that can be moved without damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do all Hanafi imams allow division of movable property claimed as inheritance without requiring evidence?
A) Because movable property is more valuable than real estate.
B) Because movable property can deteriorate quickly, so prompt division is needed.
C) Because movable property is not subject to inheritance laws.
D) Because witnesses are not available for movable property.

Key Takeaway
For movable property claimed as inheritance, the Hanafi school permits immediate division without evidence due to the risk of perishability, with all three imams in agreement.

Division on Claim of Ownership Without Explanation of Transfer
Ruling on dividing property when claimants assert ownership without explaining transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing property when claimants assert ownership without explaining the method of transfer, and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Ownership can be established by mere claim when no external rights are affected.

Building on prior rulings about dividing inherited or purchased property, this passage addresses a more ambiguous case: claimants simply say 'it is ours' without explaining how they came to own it. The Hanafi school holds that the judge may still partition the property based on their word, as Muslims are presumed truthful and no third-party rights are harmed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes claimants who assert ownership (ملك) but do not mention how the property transferred (انتقل) to them. They give no details about inheritance, purchase, gift, etc.
The key omission is the lack of explanation of transfer.
2
Recognise the missing element
Unlike earlier rulings where the mode of transfer was specified (e.g., inheritance, purchase), here it is absent. The ruling addresses this precise gap.
The judge does not require this information.
3
Apply the ruling
The judge divides the property among the claimants based solely on their claim of ownership. No further proof or investigation is needed.
This ruling simplifies the process and avoids deadlock.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ادعوا الملك ولم يذكروا كيف انتقل اليهم . اور اگر ملکیت کا دعوی کریں اور یہ نہ بیان کریں کہ کیسے ان کی طرف منتقل ہوئی تو ان کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے۔
If they claim ownership but do not mention how it transferred to them, then divide among them. And if they claim ownership and do not state how it transferred to them, then divide among them.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This final ruling extends the principle further: even if the claimants simply say 'this property is ours' without indicating whether it was inherited, purchased, or gifted, the judge may partition it among them. The reasoning, as implicit from previous passages, is that Muslims are presumed honest and no harm arises from dividing solely on their word. There is no external party (like a deceased) whose rights are affected. Thus, the judge can proceed with division based on the bare claim of ownership.

Key Terms
ملك (mulk): Ownership; right of possession.
انتقل (intaqala): Transferred (from one person to another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if claimants say 'this property is ours' but do not explain how they got it, the judge should:
A) Require them to produce a witness.
B) Divide it among them.
C) Refuse to divide.
D) Ask for a written document.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a mere claim of ownership suffices for the judge to partition property among the claimants, even without explaining how they obtained it.

Judicial Division with an Absent Heir
Instructions for judicial division with an absent heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi judge may divide property when an heir is absent and explain the rationale for requiring two present heirs.

Core Idea
Hanafi law permits division with absent heir if two present heirs provide proof; a proxy protects the absent heir's share.

When an heir is absent, inheritance division might seem impossible. However, Hanafi fiqh provides a practical solution: the judge can proceed if two present heirs establish key facts and a deputy is appointed. This lesson unpacks the conditions and reasoning behind this ruling, highlighting the role of testimony and the protection of the absent heir's rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Context
Understand that the judge’s division is valid (sahih) even with an absent heir, provided specific conditions are met. This is a practical concession to avoid delay.
The ruling applies to all inheritable property, not just houses.
2
List the Conditions for Judicial Division
Three conditions: (1) at least two present heirs, (2) they establish proof (bayyinah) of the deceased's death and the list of all heirs, (3) the property is in the possession of the present heirs.
The two present heirs effectively act as witnesses.
3
Explain the Requirement of Two Witnesses
The two present heirs are treated as witnesses (shahada) to the death and heir count. A single claimant is insufficient because Hanafi law requires at least two witnesses for such claims.
This avoids judgment against an absent party without sufficient proof.
4
Describe the Appointment of a Deputy (Wakil)
The judge appoints a wakil to take possession of the absent heir's share and safeguard it until the heir returns. The wakil acts as a trustee.
The deputy ensures the absent heir's property is not lost or misused.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require the absent heir's presence or explicit permission. The Hanafi view is more flexible, prioritizing practicality.
This ikhtilaf affects how inheritance courts operate in different jurisdictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حضروا رثان عند القاضي واقاما البينة على الوفاة وعدد الورثة والدار فى ايديهم ومعهم وارث غائب قسمها القاضى بطلب الحاضرين وينصب [۱۸۲۹۴۹] (۱۸) اور دوارث قاضی کے پاس حاضر ہوں اور وفات پر بعینہ قائم کریں اور ورثہ کی تعداد پر اور مکان ان کے قبضے میں ہو اور ان کے ساتھ غائب وارث ہو پھر بھی قاضی حاضرین کی طلب پر تقسیم کر دے۔ اور غائب کے لئے ایک وکیل مقرر کر دے جو اس کے حصے پر قبضہ کرے۔ دو وارث قاضی کے پاس حاضر ہو کر دو بات کرے۔ ایک تو مورث کی وفات پر بینہ قائم کرے کہ واقعی وہ مر چکا ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ کرے کہ ورثہ کی کل تعداد کتنی ہے اس پر گواہی قائم کرے۔ اور تیسری بات یہ ہے کہ گھر مطالبہ کرنے والوں کے قبضے میں ہو۔ اس صورت میں وارث غائب ہو پھر بھی قاضی گھر تقسیم کر دے گا اور جو وارث غائب ہو اس کے لئے وکیل مقرر کرے تا کہ وہ غائب کے حصے پر قبضہ کر کے اس کی حفاظت کرے اور جب غائب آجائے تو اس کے حوالے کر دے۔ ان چارشقون کی وجوہات یہ ہیں (۱) تقسیم کا مطالبہ کرنے والے دو آدمی اس لئے ہوں کہ وہ دو گواہ کے درجے میں ہو جائیں گے اور یقین کیا جا سکے گا کہ واقعی مورث مر چکا ہے۔ اور ورثہ کی تعداد اتنی ہی ہے۔ اور اگر مطالبہ کرنے والا ایک آدمی ہو تو یقین نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ مورث کی موت ہو چکی ہے۔ اور ورثہ کی تعداد اتنی ہی ہے۔ کیونکہ شہادت کی تعداد ایک نہیں ہوتی دو ہوتی ہے (۲) ایک نکتہ یہ بھی ہے کہ ایک مدعی اور دوسرا مدعی علیہ کے درجے میں ہوگا ۔ میت جو غائب ہے اس غائب کے خلاف فیصلہ نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ غائب پر فیصلہ کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کوئی مشترکہ غلام آزاد کرے اور اس کے پاس اتنا مال ہو کہ غلام کی قیمت ہو جائے تو اس پر غلام کی عادل قیمت لگائی جائے گی۔ اور اس کے شریکوں کو ان کے حصے دیئے جائیں گے۔ اور پورا غلام آزاد کرنے والے پر آزاد ہوگا۔
And when two heirs are present before the judge and establish proof of death and the number of heirs, and the house is in their possession, and there is an absent heir with them, the judge divides it at the request of those present and appoints... [2949] (18) And two heirs are present before the judge and establish proof of death and the number of heirs, and the house is in their possession, and there is an absent heir with them, then the judge will still divide at the request of the present heirs. And he will appoint a proxy for the absent one who will take possession of his share. The two heirs are present before the judge and do two things: first, establish proof of death that he has indeed died; second, testify as to the total number of heirs. And the third thing is that the house is in the possession of the claimants. In this case, even if the heir is absent, the judge will divide the house and appoint a proxy for the absent heir to take possession of and protect his share, and when the absent one returns, he will hand it over to him. The reasons for these four conditions are: (1) The two demandants are required so that they become like two witnesses, and it can be believed that the deceased has indeed died and the number of heirs is as stated. If there is only one demandant, it cannot be believed. Because testimony requires two witnesses. (2) Another point: one would be a plaintiff and the other a defendant; judgment cannot be passed against the absent person because it is not permissible to give judgment against an absent party. Footnote: The Prophet commanded: Whoever frees his share in a joint slave and has enough wealth to cover the slave’s price, the slave shall be valued at a fair price, and the partners shall be given their shares, and the slave is freed.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for judicial division in the presence of an absent heir. The judge requires at least two present heirs to establish proof of the deceased's death and the list of heirs, and that the property is in their possession. Once these conditions are met, the judge can proceed with the division and appoint a deputy (wakil) for the absent heir to take possession and safeguard his share. The commentator explains that two demandants are needed to serve as witnesses (shahada) to the facts, as a single person cannot provide sufficient proof. Also, since judgment against an absent party is not permitted in Hanafi law, the division is conducted with a representative for the absent heir. The footnote (hāshiyah) reiterates the hadith about freeing a share in a slave, used as proof for valuation.

Key Terms
وارث غائب (wārith ghāʾib): An heir who is not present at the time of division.
وكيل (wakīl): A proxy appointed to take possession and safeguard the absent heir's share.
بينة (bayyinah): Proof; testimony of two witnesses to establish death and number of heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
Hanafi judges can divide inheritance with an absent heir provided two present heirs establish proof; a proxy protects the absent heir's share.

Division of Property in Absent Heir's Possession
Ruling against division when property is in absent heir's hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing inherited property when an absent heir has possession, and explain the two reasons supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
No division of property when an absent heir holds possession — adjudicating against the absent is impermissible.

In this passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, we encounter a clear rule: if an absent heir (ghā’ib) has possession of the inherited property, the present heirs cannot demand division. The author provides two reinforcing arguments: possession signals ownership, and any division would constitute a judgment against an absentee (qaḍā’ ‘alā al-ghā’ib), which is invalid in Hanafi law. Let's unpack the reasoning behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act in question is the legal division (qismah) of inherited real estate. The ruling is clear: it is not permitted when the property is in the absent heir's possession.
The ruling is a prohibition (haram) in this specific circumstance.
2
Locate the two reasons
The passage gives two reasons: (1) possession indicates that the property belongs to the absent heir, not the present claimants; (2) dividing would be a judgment against an absentee (qaḍā’ ‘alā al-ghā’ib), which is impermissible.
The second reason is a fundamental principle of Hanafi adjudication.
3
Connect to broader Hanafi principles
The principle of qaḍā’ ‘alā al-ghā’ib is a key procedural rule: no binding decision can be made without hearing from the absent party. This protects the rights of absent heirs.
This principle applies beyond inheritance to all court proceedings.
4
Compare with other schools
Some schools allow division with proper representation for the absent heir, but the Hanafi school strictly prohibits it when the property is in the absent heir's hand.
This ruling is specific to the scenario where the absent heir holds possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان العقار فى يد الوارث الغائب او شيء منه لم يقسم [۲۹۵۱ (۲۰) اگر زمین غائب وارث کے قبضے میں ہو یا اس کا کچھ حصہ ہوتو تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جب پوری زمین یا اس کا کچھ حصہ غائب وارث کے قبضے میں ہو تو یہ قرینہ ہے کہ یہ زمین حاضر آدمیوں کی نہیں ہے۔ اگر یہ وارث ہوتے یا اس کی زمین ہوتی تو زمین اس کے قبضے میں ہونی چاہئے۔ لیکن ان کے قبضے میں نہیں ہے اس لئے تقسیم بھی نہیں ہوگی (۲) دوسرا نکتہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تقسیم کرتے ہیں تو قضا علی الغائب ہوگی جو جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے بھی تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔
And if the real estate is in the hand of the absent heir, or part of it, it is not divided. [2951 (20)] If the land is in the possession of the absent heir, or some portion of it, then it will not be divided. When the entire land or some portion of it is in the possession of the absent heir, this is an indication that this land does not belong to the present people. If they were the heirs or if it was their land, the land should have been in their possession. But it is not in their possession, therefore it will not be divided. (2) The second point is that if they divide, it would be judgment against the absentee, which is not permissible. Therefore it will not be divided.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling (حکم) regarding the division of inherited property when an absent heir has possession of the property or part of it. The ruling is that division is not permitted in such a case. The author provides two reasons. First, the fact that the property is in the absent heir's possession indicates that it does not belong to the present claimants; if it were theirs, they would have possessed it. Second, dividing the property would require adjudicating against the absentee (قضاء علی الغائب), which is impermissible in Hanafi fiqh. This ruling is a straightforward application of the principle that a judge cannot pass a binding judgment in the absence of one of the parties without proper representation. The lesson is from the section on division (کتاب القسمة) in Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, a Hanafi commentary.

Key Terms
قسمة (qismah): The legal process of dividing jointly owned property among co-owners or heirs.
غائب (ghā'ib): An heir who is not present at the time of division.
قضاء علی الغائب (qaḍā' 'alā al-ghā'ib): Judgment against an absentee; a legal principle that such judgment is impermissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is allowed if the majority consents.
B) It is not allowed.
C) It is allowed with compensation.
D) It is allowed only if all present agree.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the division of inherited property when the absent heir has possession, based on the indication of ownership and the principle that judgment cannot be passed against an absentee.

Division When Only One Heir Is Present
Ruling on division with one heir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on division of inheritance when only one heir is present and explain the two procedural reasons prohibiting it.

Core Idea
A single heir cannot trigger division; court requires both claimant and defendant.

This lesson examines a specific procedural rule in inheritance division: when only one heir appears to claim the estate, the division cannot proceed. The scholars base this on two key principles: the insufficiency of a single person's testimony and the legal necessity of having both a plaintiff and a defendant present in court. Understanding this ruling helps you see how Hanafi law protects absent heirs and maintains procedural justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is demanding division of inherited property when only one heir is present. The ruling is that such division is not permitted (haram).
This is a procedural prohibition, not a substantive one on ownership.
2
Understand the first reason: testimony analogy
A single claimant's statement is compared to testimony: one person does not meet the minimum number of witnesses (two men or one man and two women in financial matters). Therefore, a single heir's demand is not sufficient evidence to force division.
This is based on the general principle of testimony in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the second reason: plaintiff-defendant requirement
A valid court case requires both a plaintiff (mudda'i) and a defendant (mudda'a 'alayh). With only one heir present, he can only be considered a plaintiff, and the deceased is not a proper defendant (nor can absent heirs be represented without authorization). Thus no judgment can be passed.
This prevents a ruling against an absent party, which is impermissible.
4
Contrast with the case of two present heirs
If two heirs are present, one can be considered plaintiff and the other defendant (representing the deceased's estate), allowing division. The passage implies this through the contrast.
This highlights the crucial role of a proper opposing party.
5
Recall the overarching principle
Division is valid only if there is an overt indication of willingness to divide and court procedures are satisfied. Here, the missing defendant makes the procedure impossible.
This principle was established earlier in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان حضر وارث واحد لم يقسم [۲۹۵۲) (۲۱) اگر ایک وارث حاضر ہو تو تقسیم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ مثلا تین وارث تھے ان میں سے صرف ایک حاضر ہوا اور تقسیم کا مطالبہ کیا تو مال تقسیم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ایک آدمی شہادت کی تعداد پوری نہیں کرتا اس لئے اس کی بات نہیں سنی جائے گی (۲) ایک وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ مورث تو ہے نہیں اس لئے قاضی کے یہاں مدعی اور دوسرا مدعی علیہ چاہئے ۔ اگر دونوں ہوتے تو ایک کو مدعی مانتا اور دوسرے کو مورث کی جانب سے وکیل مان کر حاضر مدعی علیہ مان لیا جاتا اور فیصلہ ہو جاتا تا کہ غائب پر فیصلہ نہ ہو۔ اور یہاں ایک ہی مطالبہ کرنے والا ہے اس لئے اس کو زیادہ سے زیادہ مدعی مانیں گے۔ لیکن مدعی علیہ حاضر نہیں ہے اس لئے نہ فیصلہ ہوگا اور نہ مال تقسیم ہوگی۔ اصول گزر چکا ہے کہ بیچ بولنے کا قرینہ ہو اور قضا کی کاروائی کے مطابق ہو تو تقسیم ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔
And if only one heir is present, it is not divided. [2952) (21) If one heir is present, then division will not take place. For example, there were three heirs and only one of them came and demanded division, then the property will not be divided. One person does not complete the number required for testimony, so his statement is not heard. (2) Another reason is that the deceased is not there, so in the court there must be a plaintiff and another as defendant. If both were present, then one would be considered plaintiff and the other would be considered as a representative of the deceased, taking the present as defendant, so that judgment is not passed against the absent. But here there is only one claimant, so at most he can be considered plaintiff, but the defendant is not present, so neither a judgment will be passed nor the property divided. The principle has already passed that if there is an indication of intention to speak and it conforms to court proceedings, division will happen; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (حکم) that division of inherited property cannot take place when only one heir is present. The author gives two reasons. First, a single claimant's statement is not sufficient like testimony requires multiple witnesses. Second, a valid lawsuit requires both a plaintiff and a defendant present. If only one heir is present, he can be considered plaintiff, but there is no defendant present (since the other heirs are absent and the deceased is not a party). Thus no judgment can be rendered. The final line recalls an earlier principle: division is only valid if there is an overt indication of willingness to divide and the court procedures are satisfied.

Key Terms
وارث واحد (wārith wāhid): A single heir who is present at the time of division.
مدعی (mudda‘ī): Plaintiff; the party bringing the claim in court.
مدعی علیہ (mudda‘ā ‘alayh): Defendant; the party against whom the claim is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't a single present heir demand division of the estate?
A) He lacks sufficient testimony.
B) Absent heirs must all be present.
C) He can't be both plaintiff and defendant.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
A single heir cannot force inheritance division because court procedure requires both a plaintiff and a defendant to be present.

Dispute on Dividing Multiple Jointly Owned Houses: Separate vs Grouped Division
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division of jointly owned houses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dividing multiple jointly-owned houses and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Abu Hanifa's and Sahibayn's views.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires each house to be shared by all partners with price adjustment; Sahibayn give judges discretion to assign whole houses based on apparent equality.

This passage presents a practical dispute within the Hanafi school: how should a judge divide several jointly-owned houses among co-owners? Imam Abu Hanifa insists on dividing each house separately among all partners, then equalizing values through adjustment payments (tawāfuq). His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), allow the judge to assign whole houses to individual partners if that is more beneficial, focusing on apparent equality. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how Hanafi jurisprudence balances intrinsic fairness with practical discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
Determine exactly what is being disputed: when multiple houses are jointly owned in the same city, should each house be divided separately among all partners, or can the judge assign whole houses to individual partners?
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and its reasoning
Abu Hanifa holds that each house must be divided separately. His reasoning: houses have intrinsic qualities (location, neighbors, proximity to mosque) that affect value. Ignoring these would be unjust, so each partner must get a share in every house, with value adjustments.
He uses the example of three houses with different values due to location.
3
State Sahibayn's position and its reasoning
Sahibayn argue that the judge has discretion: if it is more beneficial for the partners, the judge may assign whole houses to individuals without adjustment, based on apparent equality. They focus on practical ease and apparent equality, not hidden qualities.
They give the judge the option to either assign whole houses or divide each house separately.
4
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, every partner ends up with shares in every house, and money changes hands to equalize values. Under Sahibayn, a partner could receive one whole house without any cash payment, even if that house is more valuable, as long as the judge deems it suitable.
The judge's discretion is broader in Sahibayn's view.
5
Note the default rule and the need for partner consent
Both sides agree that if partners voluntarily agree to a particular division, it is valid. The dispute is about the default procedure when partners do not agree. Abu Hanifa's default is separate division with tawāfuq; Sahibayn's default is left to judicial discretion.
The passage mentions that if all partners consent to taking one house each, Abu Hanifa accepts that.

صاحبین کے نزدیک ظاہری برابری کو لحوظ رکھا جائے گا باطنی خوبیوں کی طرف زیادہ توجہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔
[2953 (22)] And if there are jointly owned houses in a city, each house is divided separately in the opinion of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And the two (Sahibayn) said: if it is more beneficial for them to divide some within others, then divide them. [2953 (22)] If there are several jointly owned houses in one city, then each one will be divided separately according to the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa. And Sahibayn say: if it is appropriate for them to distribute some within others, then let them be divided. For example, there are three houses. One worth fifteen thousand dirhams near the mosque. The second worth ten thousand dirhams on the eastern side of the village. And the third house worth five thousand dirhams, a little far from the village. However, the three houses are similar in rooms and structure. And there are three partners. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the houses will be divided separately, i.e., the three will have shares in the mosque house, also in the eastern house, and also in the one far from the village. And after pricing all three houses, they will equalize. For example, the one who gets the far house worth only five thousand will be given an additional five thousand dirhams. And the person who takes the mosque house worth fifteen thousand will give five thousand dirhams to the one who gets the far house so that equalization occurs. It will not be done that all three are given one house each on the basis of apparent equality. He (Abu Hanifa) says that price differences occur due to location. For example, good neighbors and proximity to mosque increase the price. And the opposite decreases the price. Therefore, besides apparent equality, intrinsic qualities will also be considered and priced accordingly. According to Imam Azam's principle, intrinsic qualities will be considered. Yes, if the three partners agree to take one house each, then he may divide in that way. Sahibayn say that this is left to the judge's opinion. If it is suitable for them to give each one house without any additional payment, then the judge has that option even if the partners are not satisfied. And he also has the option to give all three shares in each house, then price each house and equalize. The principle of Sahibayn is that apparent equality will be considered; intrinsic qualities will not be given much attention.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-madhhab dispute (کتاب القسمة) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), regarding the division of multiple jointly-owned houses in the same city. Abu Hanifa holds that each house must be divided individually among all partners, then an adjustment payment (توافق) is made to account for differences in value due to location and other intrinsic qualities. He emphasizes considering both apparent and hidden qualities. Sahibayn give the judge discretion: if it is more beneficial, the judge can assign whole houses to individual partners without adjustment, or he can divide each house separately. Their principle focuses on apparent equality rather than intrinsic qualities. The passage uses an example of three houses with different values to illustrate the practical difference between the two positions.

Key Terms
توافق (tawāfuq): Adjustment payment made to equalize shares when properties of different values are divided.
قسمة (qismah): Division of jointly owned property.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary reason Imam Abu Hanifa insists on dividing each house separately among all partners?
A) To ensure that each partner gets a house of similar physical size
B) Because houses have intrinsic qualities (like location and neighbors) that affect value, and ignoring them is unjust
C) Because the law requires that all property must be physically divided
D) Because the judge has no authority to assign whole houses

Key Takeaway
The division of multiple jointly-owned houses in Hanafi fiqh involves a tension between substantive equality (Abu Hanifa) and judicial discretion with apparent equality (Sahibayn); both are valid and the later school may prefer practicality.

Division of Mixed Properties: Separate Types Rule
Ruling with proof on dividing mixed property types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing mixed properties of different types and apply the principle of value adjustment using the prophetic precedent.

Core Idea
Different property types are separate categories; each must be divided individually with monetary equalization.

When partners jointly own a house and land, or a house and a shop, these are considered separate types (jins). Hanafi law requires that each type be divided separately among all partners, then values equalized through monetary exchange if needed. This ruling is based on the prophetic precedent of equating ten goats to one camel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the property types
Determine if the jointly owned property consists of different types such as house, land, or shop. Each type is a separate jins.
Types differ in nature and value.
2
Recognize the default rule
Each type must be divided individually among all partners. Both partners get shares in the house and also shares in the land/shop.
This ensures each partner owns part of each type.
3
Consider mutual agreement
Partners may agree to assign whole items to individuals (e.g., one takes house, other takes land). This is permissible but requires value adjustment.
Agreement does not eliminate the need for equalization.
4
Perform value adjustment
Calculate the monetary value of each type. The partner receiving the higher-value item must pay the other half the difference to equalize shares.
Example: House 10,000, land 5,000 → house-taker pays 2,500.
5
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet equated ten goats to one camel during division. This demonstrates that different types can be exchanged with value adjustment, analogous to house and land.
Hadith from Bukhari, Book of Division of Goats.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ۲۹۵۴ (۲۳) وان كانت دار وضيعة او داروحانوت قسم كل واحدة على حدته [ ۲۹۵۴] (۲۳) اگر مکان اور زمین ہوں یا مکان اور دکان ہوں تو ہر ایک کو علیحد علیحدہ تقسیم کرے۔ مثلا دو حصے دار ہیں اور مالیت میں ایک مکان اور زمین ہے۔ تو مکان میں بھی دونوں کو حصہ دیں اور زمین میں بھی دونوں کو حصہ دیں۔ ہاں ! اگر ایک آدمی صرف مکان لینے پر اور دوسرا آدمی صرف زمین لینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو ٹھیک ہے۔ مکان الگ جنس ہے اور زمین الگ جنس ہے اور دونوں کی قیمتوں میں بہت فرق ہوتا ہے اس لئے بالا تفاق مکان میں بھی دونوں کا حصہ ہوگا اور زمین میں بھی دونوں کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ گویا کہ تبدیل اور خرید ہوگی۔ اس لئے دونوں کی قیمت لگا کر تو افق کیا جائے گا۔ مثلا مکان کی قیمت دس ہزار ہے اور زمین کی قیمت پانچ ہزار ہے۔ تو مکان لینے والے پر زمین لینے والے کو ڈھائی ہزار دینا ہو گا ۔ یہی حال مکان اور دکان کا ہے کہ دونوں دو جنس ہیں۔ عن عباية بن رفاعة بن رافع بن خديج عن جده قال كنا مع النبي الله بذي الحليفة ... ثم قسم فعدل عشرة من الغنم ببعير (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب قسمته الغنم ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۲۴۸۸) اس حدیث میں بکری الگ جنس ہے اور اونٹ الگ جنس ہے اس لئے دس بکریوں کو ایک اونٹ کے برابر کیا۔ پس کسی کو ایک اونٹ دیا تو اس سے توافق کرنے کے لئے دوسرے کو دس بکریاں دی۔ اسی طرح مکان اور دکان کا حال ہو گا۔
[2954 (23)] And if there is a house and a land or a house and a shop, divide each one separately. [2954] (23) If there are a house and land, or a house and a shop, then divide each one separately. For example, there are two partners and the assets include a house and land. Then give both partners shares in the house and also give both shares in the land. Yes, if one person agrees to take only the house and the other only the land, that is fine. The house is a separate type and the land is a separate type, and their prices differ greatly. Therefore, by consensus, both will have shares in the house and both will have shares in the land. And this is like exchange and purchase. So both will be priced and equalization will be done. For example, the house is worth ten thousand and the land five thousand. Then the one taking the house must pay the one taking the land two and a half thousand. The same applies to a house and a shop: they are two different types. From 'Abayah ibn Rifa'ah ibn Rafi' ibn Khadij from his grandfather: He said, 'We were with the Prophet, peace be upon him, at Dhu al-Hulayfah... then he divided, making ten goats equal to one camel.' (Bukhari, Book of Division of Goats, p. 1338, no. 2488) In this hadith, the goat is a separate type and the camel is a separate type, so ten goats were equated to one camel. Thus, when giving someone a camel, for equalization he gave ten goats to the other. Similarly is the case of a house and a shop.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (حکم) that when jointly owned property consists of different types (e.g., house and land, or house and shop), each type must be divided separately among the partners. The reason is that different types have different values and are considered separate categories. The author provides a prophetic proof (dalil) from the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ equated ten goats to one camel during division, indicating that different types can be exchanged with value adjustment. Similarly, in the case of house and land/shop, each partner gets a share in both items, and then a monetary adjustment is made to equalize the values. If partners agree to assign whole items to individuals, that is also permissible.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Type or category of property; different jins affect division rules.
تبدیل (tabdīl): Exchange; the process of swapping shares for monetary compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith about ten goats equal to one camel demonstrate regarding division of different types of property?
A) Different types cannot be combined in division
B) Value adjustment is necessary when dividing different types
C) Goats and camels are the same type
D) Division is allowed only with consent of all parties

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, different property types must be divided separately, and values adjusted to ensure fairness, as established by the prophetic precedent of equating goats and camels.

Duties of the Divider: Mapping, Measuring, Valuing, Separating
Procedural guidelines for the divider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four procedural duties of a qāsim in dividing jointly owned property and explain why access rights must be preserved.

Core Idea
A proper division severs all rights between co-owners, including paths and water channels.

This passage outlines the standard procedure for a divider (qāsim) when partitioning jointly owned property. The Hanafi school emphasises precise mapping, measurement, valuation, and separation of shares including easements to ensure no rights remain between co-owners.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divider and their appointment
The qāsim is an impartial person appointed by a judge or agreed upon by the co-owners. Without proper appointment, the division may be invalid.
The passage assumes a valid appointment.
2
List the four duties
The divider must: (1) draw a map of the property, (2) measure it evenly, (3) value any structures, and (4) separate each share including its path and water channel.
These are considered arkan (essentials) for a valid division.
3
Understand the purpose: eliminating residual rights
Each step ensures that after division, no co-owner has any claim over another's share. This includes rights of way and drainage.
The goal is a clean severance of joint ownership.
4
Recognize the sunnah and optional nature
Mapping (taṣwīr) is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory. However, omitting measurement or valuation may invalidate the division.
The Hanafi school treats these duties as recommended but with consequences if ignored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۵۵] (۲۴) وينبغي للقاسم ان يصوّر ما يقسم ويسوي ويقيس ويقوم العمارة ويفرد حصة كل واحد عن الاخر بطريقه ونهره حتى لا يبقى لكل واحد منهم في حصة صاحبه حق [۲۹۵۵] (۲۴) تقسیم کرنے والے کے لئے مناسب ہے کہ جس کو تقسیم کرے اس کا نقشہ بنائے اور برابر کر کے ناپ لے اور عمارت کی قیمت لگالے، اور ہر ایک کا حصہ جدا کر لے باقی سے اس کے راستے اور نالی کے ساتھ ، تا کہ ایک کے حصے کا دوسرے سے تعلق باقی نہ رہے۔ پھر ان کا حاشیہ : (الف) ہم حضور کے ساتھ ذی الحلیفہ میں تھے۔ پھر تقسیم فرمائی اور دس بکریوں کو ایک اونٹ کے برابر فرمایا۔
[2955] (24) It is appropriate for the divider to draw a map of what he divides, measure evenly, value the building, and separate each person's share from the others along with its path and water channel, so that none of them retains any right in the share of the other. [2955] (24) It is appropriate for the divider to draw a map of what he divides, measure it evenly, value the building, and separate each person's share from the rest along with its path and water channel, so that one's share does not remain connected to another's. Then their... Footnote: (a) We were with the Prophet at Dhu al-Hulayfah. Then he made a division, equating ten goats to one camel.

Commentary
This passage outlines the procedural steps (أصول القسمة) that a divider (قاسم) should follow when partitioning jointly owned property. The divider must: create a visual map (تصویر), measure the property accurately, appraise the value of any structures, and separate each shareholder's portion ensuring that access rights (path) and drainage (water channel) are clearly delineated. The goal is to eliminate any residual rights or easements one shareholder might have over another's share. This ensures a clean and final division. The footnote repeats the hadith about the Prophet equating ten goats to one camel, reinforcing the principle of value adjustment in division.

Key Terms
قاسم (qāsim): The person who performs the division of jointly owned property; can be a judge-appointed expert or a mutual agent.
تصویر (taṣwīr): Drawing a map or layout of the property.
نالی (nālī): Water channel or drainage; rights to water flow must be included in the share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) To make the division easier to record

Key Takeaway
A valid division requires mapping, measuring, valuing, and separating shares with all access rights to eliminate any residual co-ownership.

Land Classification by Water Source: Imam Muhammad's Principle
Ruling by Imam Muhammad on land classification based on water source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Muhammad's rule for classifying revived dead land as 'ushri or kharaji based on the water source, and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
The water source that irrigates dead land determines its tax status – not the surrounding land.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the classification of revived dead land (ihya al-mawat). The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'ushri and kharaji land, and the question arises: what factor decides the category of newly revived land? Imam Muhammad provides a clear principle: the source of water used for irrigation is decisive. We will study his rule and the evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Possible Categories
The act is reviving dead land (ihya al-mawat). The land can become either 'ushri (subject to tithe) or kharaji (subject to land tax). Note the legal consequences of each category.
'Ushri land is owned by the Muslim cultivator; kharaji land is state-owned and leased.
2
State Imam Muhammad's Criterion
Imam Muhammad rules that the water source used to irrigate the land determines its classification. List the two types of water sources he distinguishes.
Ownerless waters (wells, springs, great rivers) give 'ushri status; Persian-dug canals give kharaji status.
3
Analyze the Proof: Athar of Umar
Read the athar where Umar grants land in Basra. Identify the key phrase: 'no jizyah water flows to it'. Explain how this supports Imam Muhammad's principle.
The term jizyah here means kharaj, referring to land tax.
4
Apply the Rule to Examples
Test the rule: If a person digs a well on dead land, the land becomes 'ushri. If they use water from a Persian canal, it becomes kharaji. Confirm that proximity to other land types does not change the ruling.
The water source overrides location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باجماع الصحابة رضى الله عنهم [۳۰۶۱ (۸۲) وقال محمد رحمه الله تعالى ان احياها ببئر حفرها او بعين استخرجها او بماء دجلة او الفرات او الانهار العظام التي لا يملكها اصول مردہ زمین کی اصلیت کا اندازہ برابر کی زمین کس کی ملکیت ہے اس سے لگایا جائے گا۔ بصرہ ان کے یہاں عشری زمین ہے۔ اس کا اشارہ اس اثر سے ملتا ہے۔ عن محمد بن عبید الله الثقفي ، قال خرج رجل من اهل البصرة من ثقيف يقال له نافع ابو عبد الله، وكان اول من افتلا الفلا ، فقال لعمر بن الخطاب ان قبلنا ارضا بالبصرة ليست من ارض الخراج ولا تضر باحد من المسلمين فان رأيت ان تقطعنيها اتخذ فيها قضبا لخيلى فافعل، قال فكتب عمر الى ابى موسى الاشعرى ... فان لم تكن ارض جزية ولا ارضا يجرى اليها ماء جزية فاعطها اياه (الف) ( رواه عبید فی الاموال، ص ۲۷۷، اعلاء السنن، باب من احياء ارضنا مواتا بماء الخراج فخراجية والافعشریة ، ج الثانی عشر، ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۴۰۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بصرہ خراجی زمین نہیں تھی۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مردہ زمین میں خراجی پانی جائے تو وہ زمین بھی خراجی ہو جائے گی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگلے مسئلے میں امام محمد کی رائے کہ جس پانی سے سیراب کیا جائے زمین وہی شمار کی جائینگی۔ اخت چیز : اردگرد، برابر کی زمین ۔ [۳۰۶۱ (۸۲) امام محمد نے فرمایا اگر زمین کو زندہ کیا کنواں کھود کر یا چشمہ نکال کر یا دجلہ یا فرات یا ان بڑی نہروں کے پانی سے جن کا کوئی مالک نہیں ہے تو وہ عشری ہے۔ اور اگر زندہ کیا ان نہروں کے پانی سے جن کو عجمیوں نے کھودا ہے جیسے نہر ملک اور نہریز دجر د تو وہ خراجی ہے۔ امام محمد کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ پانی کس قسم کا استعمال کرتا ہے اس کے اعتبار سے مردہ زمین خراجی یا عشری ہوگی۔ پس اگر خراجی پانی ڈال کر مردہ زمین کو زندہ کیا تو وہ زمین خراجی ہوگی چاہے وہ عشری زمین کے درمیان : و۔ اور اگر عشری پانی ڈال کر زندہ کیا تو وہ عشری ہوگی۔ آگے تفصیل ہے کہ کون سا پانی عشری ہے اور کون ساخراجی ہے۔ کسی نے خود کنواں کھودایا چشمہ نکالا تو ان دونوں کا پانی عشری ہے۔ اس سے مردہ زمین زندہ کیا تو زمین عشری ہوگی۔ یا نہر دجلہ، نہر فرات یا وہ نہر جن کا کوئی مالک نہیں اس کا پانی عشری ہے اس لئے اس پانی سے جو مردہ زمین زندہ کرے گا وہ عشری ہوگی۔ ے دو۔ اور وہ نہر جس کو عجمیوں نے کھودا ہو جیسے نہر ملک اور نہریز و جر دان کا پانی خراجی ہے۔ اس پانی سے مردہ زمین زندہ کرے گا تو وہ خراجی ہوگی۔ اوپر حضرت عمر کا اثر گزرا۔ فان لم تكن ارض جزية ولا ارضا يجرى اليها ماء جزية فاعطها اياه (ب)(رواه عبيد فى الاموال، ص ۷ ۲۷، اعلاء السفن، نمبر ۴۰۹ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بصرہ کی اس زمین میں جزیہ یعنی خراجی پانی نہ جاتا ہو تو نافع ابوعبید اللہ کو ۔ حاشیہ : (الف) محمد بن عبید اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بصرہ کا ایک آدمی ثقیف سے نکلا جس کا نام نافع ابو عبد اللہ تھا۔ یہ پہلا آدمی ہے جس نے جنگل میں میدان بنایا ۔ پس عمر بن خطاب سے کہا مجھ سے پہلے بصرہ میں خراجی زمین نہیں ہے اور مسلمانوں کو نقصان دیتی ہے۔ پس اگر مجھے زمین کچھ ٹکڑا دیں جس میں گھوڑے کے دوڑنے کی جگہ بناؤں تو کرلوں نے پس حضرت عمر نے حضرت ابو موسی اشعری کو لکھا. اگر جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اور نہ ایسی زمین ہو جس میں جزیہ کا پانی جاری ہوتا ہو تو اس کو عطا کر دو۔ (ب) اگر جزیہ کی زمین نہ ہو اور نہ اس میں جزیہ کا پانی جاری ہوتا ہو تو اس کو عطا کر دو۔ احد فهي عُشريّة وان احياها بماء الانهار التي احتفرها الاعاجم مثل نهر الملک ونهر یزدجرد فهى خراجيّة اس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے خراجی زمین بننے میں پانی کا اعتبار ہے قرب وجوار کا اعتبار نہیں۔ لفت انظر : حضر سے مشتق ہے کھودنا۔
Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If he revives it by digging a well, or extracting a spring, or with the water of the Tigris, the Euphrates, or the great rivers that no one owns, then it is 'ushri. And if he revives it with the water of rivers that the Persians dug, such as Nahr al-Malik and Nahr Yazdegerd, then it is kharaji. The athar: From Muhammad ibn 'Ubayd Allah al-Thaqafi: A man from Basra called Nafi' Abu 'Abd Allah, the first to clear the land, said to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'We have land in Basra that is not kharaj land and harms no Muslim. If you see fit to grant it to me, I will make a racetrack for my horses.' So 'Umar wrote to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'If it is not jizyah land and no jizyah water flows to it, then give it to him.' (Reported by 'Ubayd in al-Amwal, p. 277; I'la' al-Sunan, vol. 12, p. 225, no. 409).
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the classification of revived dead land (ihya al-mawat). The core principle is that the water source used for irrigation determines the legal status of the land: 1) If the water comes from a personally dug well, a natural spring, or from great ownerless rivers like the Tigris and Euphrates, the land becomes 'ushri (tithe land). 2) If the water comes from canals dug by Persian kings (e.g., Nahr al-Malik or Nahr Yazdegerd), the land is kharaji (subject to land tax). Imam Muhammad's rule is based on the practical effect of the water's origin, not the location of the land; even 'ushri land surrounded by kharaji land becomes kharaji if irrigated with kharaji water. The proof is the historical precedent of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) granting land in Basra which was not kharaj land and had no kharaj water flowing to it, making it 'ushri. This indicates that the water's nature determines the land's category. The commentary explains that the water's ownership and source are determinative, not the surrounding area.

Key Terms
إحياء الموات (ihya' al-mawat): Reviving dead land by making it cultivable through irrigation or construction.
عشري ('ushri): Land subject to 'ushr (tithe) tax, typically owned by Muslims and irrigated by natural or private sources.
خراجي (kharaji): Land subject to kharaj (land tax), typically conquered land or land irrigated by state-controlled water.
جزية (jizyah): In this context, jizyah refers to the land tax (kharaj), as seen in 'Umar's usage 'mau jizyah' meaning water of kharaj land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what determines whether revived dead land becomes 'ushri or kharaji?
A) The location of the land relative to other 'ushri or kharaji land.
B) The water source used to irrigate the land.
C) The permission of the ruling authority.
D) The type of crop planted.

Key Takeaway
The water source used to irrigate revived dead land determines its classification as 'ushri or kharaji in the Hanafi school.

The Apostate's Property: Suspended Ownership (Zawal Mura'a)
Ruling with proof on the suspended nature of apostate's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the apostate's property and explain the concept of suspended ownership (zawal mura'a) using the dalil provided.

Core Idea
An apostate's ownership is suspended, not lost; if he returns to Islam, it is restored; if he dies, it goes to Muslim heirs.

This passage introduces a unique Hanafi concept: the property of an apostate is not immediately and irrevocably lost. Instead, it enters a state of suspension (zawal mura'a), which can be reversed by repentance. Two textual proofs establish this ruling: a hadith about a man who married his stepmother and a companion athar (report) from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). Understanding this suspended status is crucial for correctly applying inheritance and property laws in cases of apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage states that the apostate's ownership ceases with a suspended cessation (zawal mura'a). Note the term: it is not an absolute removal but a conditional one.
2
Understand the condition for reversal
If the apostate returns to Islam, his ownership is restored to its original state. This shows that the suspension is reversible.
The Hanafi school gives the apostate an opportunity to repent, typically three days.
3
Examine the first proof (hadith)
The hadith of the stepmother marriage: the Prophet ordered the execution and confiscation of property. This shows that if the apostate is executed, his property is taken, implying loss of ownership. However, the passage uses this to support that upon death, the property is distributed among Muslim heirs, not that loss is immediate.
The hadith alone does not prove suspended status but combined with the athar, it supports the Hanafi view.
4
Examine the second proof (athar of Ali)
Ali executed an apostate and divided his inheritance among Muslim heirs. This demonstrates that the property acquired during Islam is inheritable, while property acquired during apostasy becomes booty (ghanimah).
The athar clarifies the distribution upon death and implies the suspension before death.
5
Distinguish between pre- and post-apostasy property
The passage specifies that property acquired during Islam is divided among Muslim heirs, while property acquired during apostasy becomes booty. This distinction applies if the apostate dies without repentance. If he repents, all property is restored.
This shows that the suspension does not affect the nature of the property permanently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويزول ملك المرتد عن امواله بردّته زوالا مراعى فان اسلم عادت املاکه الی حالها. مرتد کی ملکیت زائل ہو جائے گی اس کے مال سے مرتد ہونے کی وجہ سے محفوظ زوال، پس اگر اسلام لایا تو اپنی حالت پر لوٹ جائیگی۔ مرتد ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی ملکیت زائل ہو جائے گی ۔ لیکن اس انداز میں زائل ہوگی کہ اگر دوبارہ اسلام لے آیا تو ملکیت بحال رہے گی ۔ اور اگر مر گیا تو وہ مال مسلمان ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ سوتیلی ماں سے نکاح کر کے مرتد ہوا تو اس کو قتل کرنے اور اس کے مال کو لے لینے کا حکم دیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن یزید صلى الله بن البراء عن ابيه قال لقينى عمى وقد اعتقد راية فقلت اين تريد قال بعثني رسول الله له الى رجل نكح امرأة ابيه ان اضرب عنقه و آخذ ماله (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب مال المرتد از امات اقتل على الردة ، ج عامن ص ۱۳۶۱ نمبر ۱۶۸۹۳ ارابن ماجته شریف ، باب من تزوج امرأة ابيه من بعده، ص ۳۷۵، نمبر (۲۶۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد ہو جائے تو اس کو قتل کیا جائے گا اور مال لے لیا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن على انه اتى بمستورد العجلى وقد ارتد فعرض عليه الاسلام فابي قال فقتله وجعل ميراثه بين ورثته المسلمين (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ۳۲ ، ما قالوانی المرقد ما جاء فی میراثہ ، ج سادس، ص ۴۴۵، نمبر ۳۲۷۵۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد ہوتے ہی اس کی ملیکت زائل ہو جائے گی۔ البتہ اسلام پیش کرنے اور اسلام لانے تک انتظار کیا جائے گا۔ اگر اسلام نہیں لایا تو مکمل طور پر ملکیت زائل ہو جائے گی۔ اور اسلام کے زمانے میں کمایا ہوا مال مسلمان ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو گا اور کفر کے زمانے میں کمایا ہوا مال غنیمت ہوگا۔ اور اگر اسلام لے آیا تو اس کا مال واپس دیا جائے گا۔ مرید دوبارہ اسلام لے آئے تو اس کا مال واپس دیا جائے گا۔
And the ownership of the apostate over his property ceases by his apostasy with a suspended cessation; if he becomes Muslim, his properties return to their previous state. The ownership of the apostate will be removed from his property due to apostasy as a suspended removal. So if he becomes Muslim, it will return to its state. Because of apostasy, his ownership is removed, but in a way that if he comes back to Islam, the ownership is restored. And if he dies, that property will be divided among the Muslim heirs. In a hadith, a man married his stepmother and apostatized, so the order was given to kill him and take his property. The hadith: from Yazid... that the Prophet sent me to a man who married his father's wife to strike his neck and take his property. From this hadith, it is understood that if he apostatizes, he will be killed and his property taken. And in an athar: from Ali, that Mustawrid al-Ijli was brought to him, and he had apostatized; he presented Islam to him, but he refused; so he killed him and made his inheritance among the Muslim heirs. From this athar, it is understood that as soon as he apostatizes, his ownership is removed. However, he is given the opportunity to accept Islam, and his ownership is suspended until then. If he does not become Muslim, the ownership is completely removed. Property acquired during Islam will be divided among the Muslim heirs, and property acquired during apostasy will be booty (ghanimah). And if he returns to Islam, his property will be returned to him.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi concept of suspended ownership (zawal mura'a) for an apostate. Upon apostasy, the apostate's ownership of his property does not immediately and irrevocably cease; instead, it is in a state of suspension. This means that if he returns to Islam within the period he is given (typically three days for male apostates), his ownership is fully restored. If he dies or is executed while in apostasy, his property is distributed: what he acquired during his time as a Muslim goes to his Muslim heirs, and what he acquired during apostasy becomes fay' (booty) for the Muslim treasury. The passage provides two proofs: (1) a hadith about a man who married his stepmother and apostatized — the Prophet ordered his execution and the confiscation of his property, indicating that execution removes ownership entirely. (2) An athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who executed an apostate and divided his estate among Muslim heirs. The commentary explains that the property acquired before apostasy is considered the property of a Muslim and thus inheritable by Muslim heirs, while property acquired after apostasy is considered like the gain of a harbi (enemy combatant) and thus becomes ghanimah. The passage type is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli).

Key Terms
زوال مراعى (zawal mura'a): Suspended cessation; ownership is removed but can be reinstated if the condition (return to Islam) is met.
مرتد (murtadd): A male apostate from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the property of an apostate if he returns to Islam?
A) His property remains confiscated.
B) His property is restored to him as if apostasy never occurred.
C) His property is divided among Muslim heirs.
D) His property becomes booty for the state.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that an apostate's ownership is in a state of suspended cessation (zawal mura'a), restored upon repentance or transferred to Muslim heirs upon death.

Distribution of Apostate's Property: The Period Distinction
Ruling with proof: temporal distinction in apostate's estate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for dividing an apostate's property, distinguishing between pre- and post-apostasy acquisitions, and cite the athar from Ali (RA) as proof.

Core Idea
Property earned before apostasy is inherited; property earned after apostasy is fay'.

When a person apostatizes and then dies or is executed, his property does not all become booty. The Hanafi school makes a critical temporal distinction: what he earned while a Muslim remains in the realm of inheritance for his Muslim heirs, while what he earned after apostasy is treated as spoils of war. This ruling is based on the practice of Ali (RA) and a hadith about the man who married his stepmother.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the death or execution of an apostate. The ruling is that his property is divided into two categories based on the time of acquisition.
This is not a single hukm but a distribution rule.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Ali (RA) who executed an apostate and divided his inheritance among Muslim heirs, implying the property was considered inheritable.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar shows that the apostate's property was distributed as inheritance, which indicates it must have been property acquired while he was still a Muslim. Post-apostasy property is analogized to booty because the apostate is treated as a harbi.
The distinction is not explicit in the athar but derived by legal reasoning (qiyas).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may not make this temporal distinction, treating all property as one category or giving the state a share in all.
The Hanafi position is based on the special status of the apostate as a harbi for property purposes.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is the distinction, as it combines the athar and the analogy to war booty.
No significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان مات او قتل على ردّته انتقل ما اكتسبه في حال الاسلام الى ورثته المسلمين وكان ما اكتسبه في حال ردّته فينا. اگر وہ مرگی یا مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں قتل کیا گیا تو اسلام کی حالت میں جو کچھ کمایا وہ اس کے مسلمان ورثہ میں منتقل ہو جائے گا، اور اس کی کمائی مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں غنیمت ہوگی۔ مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں مرگیا یا مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں قتل کیا گیا تو جو کچھ مسلمان ہونے کی حالت میں کمایا تھا وہ اس کے مسلمان ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوگا۔ اور جو کچھ مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں کمایا تھا وہ مال غنیمت شمار ہو گا۔ مسلمان ہونے کی حالت کی کمائی مسلمان ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ اوپر کے اثر میں گزرگئی۔ عـن علـى ... قال فقتله وجعل ميراثه بين ورثته المسلمين (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ نمبر ۳۲۷۵۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ مرتد کی کمائی مسلمان ورثہ کے درمیان تقسیم ہوگی (۲) مرتد ہونا گویا کہ مرجانا ہے۔ اور مرنے کے بعد اس کا مال ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کا مال بھی ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوگا۔ مرتد کے زمانے میں جو مال کمایا وہ غنیمت ہوگا۔ مرتد ہونے کے بعد وہ حربی ہو گیا اور حربی کا کمایا ہوا مال ہاتھ آجائے تو وہ غنیمت کا مال شمار ہوتا ہے اس لئے مرتد کے زمانے کا مال غنیمت ہو گا (۲) مسئلہ نمبر ۷ ۱۰ میں حدیث گزری کہ سوتیلی ماں سے نکاح کر کے مرتد ہوا تھا تو اس کو قتل کیا اور اس کا مال لے لیا گیا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ تھا۔ بعثنی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الى رجل نكح امرأة ابيه ان اضرب عنقه و آخذ مالہ (ج) (سن للبیہقی ،نمبر۱۶۸۹۳) جس میں تھا کہ اس کا مال لیکر غنیمت بنالیا جائے۔
And if he dies or is killed in his apostasy, what he acquired during Islam transfers to his Muslim heirs, and what he acquired during his apostasy is fay'. If he dies or is killed while in the state of apostasy, then whatever he earned while Muslim will be transferred to his Muslim heirs, and his earnings during apostasy will be booty. The proof for the division of Muslim-period earnings among Muslim heirs is the previously mentioned athar from Ali... he killed him and made his inheritance among the Muslim heirs. In this athar, the apostate's earnings are divided among Muslim heirs. (2) Apostasy is like death; after death, his property is divided among heirs. Therefore, his property will be divided among heirs. The property earned during apostasy will be booty. After apostasy, he becomes a harbi (enemy combatant), and property earned by a harbi that comes into Muslim hands is considered booty. So the property from the apostasy period is booty. (2) In issue 107, the hadith about the man who married his stepmother and apostatized is mentioned; he was killed and his property taken. The hadith fragment: 'The Messenger of Allah sent me to a man who married his father's wife to strike his neck and take his property.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) which indicated that his property was taken as booty.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage details the distribution of an apostate's property if he dies or is executed while in apostasy. The key distinction is based on the time of acquisition: property earned during his time as a Muslim (i.e., before apostasy) is treated as inheritance and passes to his Muslim heirs. Property earned after apostasy is considered fay' (booty) because the apostate is effectively in a state of war (harbi) from the moment of apostasy. The proof is the athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who executed an apostate and distributed his estate among the Muslim heirs, implying that only the property from the Muslim period is inheritable. The commentary further explains the reasoning: apostasy is analogized to death in terms of severing the link to the Muslim community, but with the added dimension of hostility, so post-apostasy gains are akin to spoils of war. The passage type is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli).

Key Terms
فىء (fay'): Booty or spoils that belong to the Muslim treasury; here, property acquired by the apostate after apostasy.
حربي (harbi): An enemy combatant from the dar al-harb; after apostasy, the apostate is treated as harbi for property purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the fate of property an apostate earned while a Muslim, if he dies in apostasy?
A) It becomes fay' for the state.
B) It is divided among his Muslim heirs.
C) It is given to his non-Muslim relatives.
D) It is destroyed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides an apostate's estate based on when property was acquired: pre-apostasy goes to heirs, post-apostasy is fay'.
