Exception: Legatee Dies Before Acceptance
States exception to the rule of acceptance for bequest ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception when a legatee dies before acceptance and explain why ownership transfers to his heirs.

Core Idea
If a legatee dies before accepting, his heirs inherit the bequest by operation of law.

This lesson examines a specific exception to the general rule that acceptance is required for ownership of a bequest. According to the Hanafi school, if the testator dies and then the legatee dies before accepting, the bequeathed property passes to the legatee's heirs as inheritance. This ruling is based on an athar from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its exception
The act is a bequest (wasiyya). The general rule is that the legatee must accept ownership. The exception: when the testator dies and then the legatee dies before acceptance, ownership passes to the legatee's heirs by inheritance.
This is not a case of rejection; the legatee simply died before having the opportunity to accept.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from 'Ali (ra): 'About a man who bequeathed to a man, and the legatee died before it reached him; he said: It belongs to the legatee's heirs.' This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah and Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
The athar is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit ruling of 'Ali indicates that the legatee's right to the bequest is established at the testator's death, even without acceptance. That right then passes to his heirs by inheritance.
Hanafi usul holds that qawl sahabi is a valid source when it does not contradict qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) generally require acceptance for validity of a bequest. According to them, if the legatee dies before acceptance, the property reverts to the testator's heirs. The Hanafi position is an exception.
The Hanafi school relies on the athar to override the general rule.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author presents this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, supported by the explicit athar. The mufta bihi is that ownership transfers to the legatee's heirs.
This is from the established corpus (zahir al-riwayah).

[13147] (10) Except in one issue: that the testator dies, then the legatee dies before acceptance; then it becomes owned by inheritance by the legatee's heirs. When the testator made the will, the legatee was alive. (c) Hadrat 'Ali said: A man bequeathed to a man, and the legatee died before the property came; what is it? He said: It will be for the legatee's heirs.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting an exception to the general rule that acceptance is needed for ownership. The exception is when the testator dies and then the legatee dies before accepting: the bequeathed property passes to the legatee's heirs as inheritance, even without acceptance. The commentary explains the scenario: the legatee was alive at the time of the will but died before accepting, and the testator died thereafter. The proof is from an athar of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who gave this ruling. This shows that the legatee's right to the property is established at the time of the testator's death, and if the legatee dies before acceptance, his heirs inherit that right.

Key Terms
وارث (wārith): Heir; one who inherits property from a deceased person.
وصیت (waṣiyya): Bequest; a will by which a person gives property to another after death.
موصی (mūṣī): Testator; the person who makes the will.
موصی له (mūṣā lahu): Legatee; the person to whom the bequest is made.
قبول (qabūl): Acceptance; the legatee's act of accepting the bequest.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, if a legatee dies before acceptance, the bequest does not lapse but passes to his heirs by inheritance, based on the athar of 'Ali (ra).

Introduction to Fara'id and the Ten Male Heirs
Introduction to Fara'id and list of ten male heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of fara'id, list the ten agreed-upon male heirs, and distinguish between paternal and maternal grandfather and types of mawla.

Core Idea
Fara'id is a communal obligation; the ten male heirs are agreed upon by consensus.

This lesson opens the book of inheritance (fara'id) with a clear definition and scriptural evidence. It then enumerates the ten male heirs whose right to inherit is universally accepted in the Hanafi school, providing necessary clarifications on terms like 'grandson', 'grandfather', and 'master'. Understanding this foundation is essential for all inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Definition and Evidence of Fara'id
Read the opening note: fara'id are fixed shares determined by Allah. The Quranic verses (4:11,12) and hadith (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah) establish its importance as a communal obligation (fard kifayah).
The principle of 'al-aqrab fa'l-aqrab' from Quran 8:75 guides heir precedence.
2
Memorize the Ten Male Heirs
Recite the list: son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, nephew, paternal uncle, paternal cousin, husband, and freeing master. Each is defined with specific conditions (e.g., 'however low' for grandson).
This list is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon across madhhabs.
3
Clarify Ambiguous Terms
Ibn al-ibn includes all male descendants through sons. Al-jadd here means paternal grandfather only; maternal grandfather is not a Quranic heir. Mawla al-ni'mah is the freeing master, distinct from mawla muwalat (client) who does not inherit.
The author uses 'abu al-ab' to stress paternal lineage.
4
Apply the Principle of Preference
Note that heirs are not equal; the nearer excludes the farther. For instance, a son blocks the grandson, and a father blocks the grandfather. This 'al-aqrab fa'l-aqrab' rule is derived from Quran 8:75.
Details of exclusion (hajb) will be covered in later lessons.

Al-jadd: in Arabic, it refers both to paternal grandfather and maternal grandfather. One is mawla muwalat: if a person becomes Muslim at the hand of someone or makes an oath and promises to live together for life, he is called mawla muwalat; he does not inherit. Commentary
This passage introduces the science of inheritance (fara'id) and lists the ten male heirs on whose inheritance there is consensus. The opening defines fara'id as the determination of fixed shares by Allah, supported by Quranic verses (Surah an-Nisa 4:11-12) and a hadith urging learning and teaching these rulings. The principle of preference (al-aqrab fa'l-aqrab) from Surah al-Anfal 8:75 is also cited. The ten heirs are then enumerated: son, grandson (however low), father, grandfather (however high), brother, nephew, paternal uncle, paternal cousin, husband, and the freeing master. The commentary explains each: ibn al-ibn refers to the son's son (grandson), and 'however low' includes great-grandsons. Al-jadd (grandfather) is clarified as paternal grandfather (father's father) because maternal grandfather is not a Quranic heir but a dhawi al-arham. Mawla is divided into two types: mawla muwalat (client by alliance) who does not inherit except in absence of all heirs, and mawla 'itaqah (client by manumission) who inherits. The passage is cut off mid-explanation of the latter.

Key Terms
فرائض (fara'id): The plural of faridah; the science of fixed shares in inheritance as determined by Allah in the Quran.
ابن الابن (ibn al-ibn): Son's son (grandson), including descendants however low, i.e., great-grandson, etc.
الجد (al-jadd): In this context, it means paternal grandfather (father's father), excluding maternal grandfather.
مولی النعمة (mawla al-ni'mah): The master who freed a slave; he inherits from the freed slave if there are no other heirs.

Defining Faraid and Its Scriptural Foundations
Opens the Book of Faraid with definition, Quran and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of faraid and identify its Quranic and Hadith proofs, applying the principle of al-aqrab fal-aqrab.

Core Idea
Faraid are fixed shares from Allah; learning them is a collective obligation.

This lesson opens the Book of Faraid (inheritances) by defining the term and establishing its scriptural basis. You will learn why the science of inheritance is called faraid, and see the primary Quranic verses and a hadith that obligate its study. Understanding these proofs is essential before diving into the detailed rules of distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and technical definition of faraid
Faraid (plural of faridah) linguistically means 'to determine' and technically refers to the fixed shares of inheritance ordained by Allah.
2
Locate the Quranic proof (dalil naqli)
The passage cites Surah an-Nisa 4:11-12, which explicitly lays out the shares for children, spouses, and parents. The imperative 'yusikum' indicates the obligation of these rules.
The imperative form in Arabic (يوصيكم) signals a binding command in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the Hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Hurairah (RA) commands the learning and teaching of faraid, making it a fard kifayah (collective obligation) on the community.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah; its authenticity supports the obligation.
4
Extract the principle of al-aqrab fal-aqrab
From Surah al-Anfal 8:75, the principle that closer relatives take precedence over more distant ones is derived – this orders residuary heirs (asabah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
ضروری نوٹ فرائض فریضہ کی جمع ہے، اس کا معنی ہے متعین کرنا۔ چونکہ اس میں ورثہ کے حصے اللہ نے متعین فرمایا ہے اس لئے اس کو فرائض کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت میں ہے۔ يوصيكم الله في اولادكم للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين فان كن نساء فوق اثنتين فلهن ثلثا ماترك وان كانت واحدة فلها النصف الخ (الف) (آیت اا، سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت اور اس کے بعد کی آیت میں بہت سے وارثین کے حصے بیان کئے گئے ہیں۔ حصوں کی تفصیل کی لئے سورۃ النساء کی آیت نمبر ۱۱ ۱۲ اور ۶ ۷ اضرور ایک مرتبہ پڑھ لیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله تعلموا الفرائض والقرن وعلموا الناس فانی مقبوض (ب) ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تعلیم الفرائض ، ص ۲۹، نمبر ۲۰۹ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب الحث على تعليم الفرائض ، ص ۱۳۹۶ نمبر ۲۷۱۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرائض سیکھے اور لوگوں کو سکھلائے تا کہ صحیح طور پر وراثت تقسیم کر سکے۔
فرائض میں بعض بعض پر مقدم ہوں گے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ واولوا الارحام بعضهم اولى ببعض في كتاب الله (ج)
(آیت ۷۵ ، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں الاقرب فالا قرب کا اصول بیان کیا گیا ہے۔
The Book of Faraid. Necessary note: Faraid is the plural of faridah, its meaning is to determine. Because in it the shares of the heirs are determined by Allah, that is why it is called faraid. Its proof is in this verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male a share equal to that of two females, and if they are women above two, then for them two-thirds of what he leaves, and if she is one, then for her half...' etc. (a) (Verse 11, Surah an-Nisa 4). In this verse and the verse after it, the shares of many heirs are stated. For the details of shares, one must read once the verses number 11, 12, and 6, 7 of Surah an-Nisa. (2) In a hadith: From Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Learn the faraid and the Quran and teach the people, for I am about to be taken.' (b) (Tirmidhi, Jami' at-Tirmidhi, chapter on teaching faraid, p.29, no. 209, and Ibn Majah, Sunan Ibn Majah, chapter on urging to teach faraid, p.1396, no. 2719). From this hadith it is known that faraid should be learned and taught to others so that inheritance may be correctly distributed. In faraid, some are given precedence over others. The proof of this is this verse: 'But those of kinship are closer to one another in the decree of Allah.' (c) (Verse 75, Surah al-Anfal 8). In this verse, the principle of al-aqrab fal-aqrab (the nearest then the next nearest) is stated.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Faraid in the Sharh. It first defines the term 'faraid' linguistically and technically, then provides scriptural proofs for the obligation of learning and implementing the laws of inheritance. The definition: faraid is the plural of faridah, meaning a fixed share. The technical subject is the determination of the shares of heirs as fixed by Allah. The primary proof is the Quranic verses from Surah an-Nisa (4:11-12 and also 4:176) which explicitly detail the shares of children, spouses, and parents. The passage also cites a hadith from Abu Hurairah commanding the learning and teaching of faraid, indicating its collective obligation (fard kifayah) in the Hanafi school. Additionally, the principle of preferring closer relatives (al-aqrab fal-aqrab) is derived from Surah al-Anfal (8:75). This principle is the foundation for determining which heirs are entitled and in what order. The commentary then transitions to the enumeration of heirs.

Key Terms
الفريضة (al-faridah): The fixed share of an heir in inheritance, as determined by Allah.
الفرائض (al-faraid): The plural of faridah; the science of inheritance law.
الاقرب فالاقرب (al-aqrab fal-aqrab): The principle that closer relatives take precedence over more distant ones in inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence cited for the fixed shares of heirs?
A) Surah al-Baqarah 2:180
B) Surah an-Nisa 4:11-12
C) Surah al-Anfal 8:75
D) Surah an-Nur 24:32

Key Takeaway
Faraid is the science of fixed inheritance shares; its study is a collective obligation supported by the Quran and Sunnah, and the principle of al-aqrab fal-aqrab governs the order of heirs.

The 17 Heirs by Consensus
Enumerates the 17 consensus heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the ten male and seven female heirs who inherit by consensus and explain the scope of inclusive terms like ibn al-ibn and al-jadd.

Core Idea
Seventeen heirs are agreed upon: ten male and seven female; all others are excluded or remote.

This passage serves as a foundational memorization anchor in Hanafi faraid. It lists the heirs whose right to inherit is established by consensus (ijma) across all madhahib. Understanding this list is the first step in identifying who inherits and who is excluded.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Ten Male Heirs
List in order: son, son's son (and any male descendant through males), father, paternal grandfather (father's father, even higher), brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, husband, and the master who freed a slave (mawla al-ni'mah).
The phrase 'wa in safala' for son's son means all male agnatic descendants, however low.
2
Memorize the Seven Female Heirs
List: daughter, son's daughter (and any female descendant through males), mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and the female master who freed a slave (mawlat al-ni'mah).
The grandmother here includes both paternal and maternal grandmother? The passage is ambiguous; details come later.
3
Interpret 'Ibn al-Ibn wa in Safala'
This term includes all male descendants through the male line, not just the immediate grandson. For example, if the deceased has no son, the grandson inherits; if no grandson, the great-grandson inherits, and so on.
This is an important principle: male agnatic descendants are never cut off as long as a male line exists.
4
Interpret 'Al-Jadd Abu al-Ab'
The grandfather mentioned here is specifically the paternal grandfather. The maternal grandfather is not included because he is from dhawi al-arham (distant relatives) and does not inherit as a regular heir.
The clarification is necessary because the word 'jadd' in Arabic can mean both paternal and maternal grandfather.
5
Understand Mawla al-Ni'mah
This is the master who frees a slave; he inherits from the freed slave by virtue of wala' (patronage). There is also a mawla muwalat (by pact), but that category does not inherit except in absence of all other heirs.
Wala' is a distinct cause of inheritance unique to the relationship between manumitter and freed slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجمع على توريثهم من الذكور عشرة (ا) الابن و (۲) ابن الابن وان سفل و (۳) الاب و (۴) الجدابو الاب وان علا (۵) والاخ و (۲) ابن الاخ و (۷) العم و ( ۸ ) ابن العم و (۹) الزوج و (۱۰) مولى النعمة 
ابن الابن : بیٹے کا بیٹا ، جس کو اردو میں پوتا کہتے ہیں، 'وان سفل' کا معنی یہ ہے کہ پوتا نہ ہو تو پڑپوتا کو وراثت ملے گی۔ اور اگر پڑپوتا نہ ہو تو سرپوتا کو وراثت ملے گی، الجد : عربی میں جد دادا کو بھی کہتے ہیں اور نانا کو بھی کہتے ہیں۔ اس لئے مصنف نے ابو الاب کہہ کر بات صاف کی کہ یہاں دادا مراد ہے نانا مراد نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ذوی الارحام میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو وراثت نہیں ملتی۔ کوئی وارث نہ ہو تو اخیر میں نانا یا ماموں کو مال دے دیا جاتا ہے، مولی النعمة : مولی کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک مولی موالات، کوئی آدمی کسی کے ہاتھ پر مسلمان ہو یا کسی کے ساتھ قسم کھا کر زندگی بھر ساتھ رہنے کا وعدہ کرے تو وہ مولی موالات کہلاتا ہے اس کو وراثت نہیں ملتے۔ ہاں کوئی وارث نہ ہو تو آخیر میں اس کو مال دے دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور دوسرا وہ آتا ہے جس نے غلام کو آزاد کیا اس کو مولی عتاقہ یا مولی العمہ کہتے ہیں۔ وہ غلام کا وارث ہوتا ہے۔ یہاں مولی النعمہ سے آزاد کرنے والا آقا مراد ہے۔

ومن الاناث سبع (ا) البنت و (۲) بنت الابن و (۳) الام و (۲) الجدة و (۵) الاخت و (۲) الزوجة و (۷) مولاة النعمة
یہ سات قسم کی عورتیں وارث بنتی ہیں جس پر اجماع ہے، اس کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔
بنت الابن : بیٹے کی بیٹی جس کو اردو میں پوتی کہتے ہیں، مولاۃ النعمتہ : وہ عورت جس نے اپنے غلام کو آزاد کیا ہو تو اس آزاد کردہ غلام کی وراثت آقا یعنی سیدہ کو ملے گی۔ اس کو مولاۃ النعمہ یا مولاۃ العتاقہ کہتے ہیں ۔ ہر ایک کی دلیل آگے آرہی ہے۔
Those upon whom there is consensus regarding their inheritance from the males are ten: (1) the son, (2) the son's son, even if lower, (3) the father, (4) the grandfather, i.e., the father's father, even if higher, (5) the brother, (6) the brother's son, (7) the paternal uncle, (8) the paternal uncle's son, (9) the husband, (10) the master of grace (the manumitter). 
Ibn al-ibn: son's son, called pota in Urdu; 'wa in safala' means that if there is no grandson (son's son), then the great-grandson inherits, and if no great-grandson, then the great-great-grandson. Al-jadd: in Arabic, jadd means both paternal grandfather and maternal grandfather; so the author clarified by saying 'abu al-ab' that here the paternal grandfather is meant, not the maternal grandfather, because the latter is from among the dhawi al-arham and does not inherit; if there is no heir, then eventually the maternal grandfather or maternal uncle gets the property. Mawla al-ni'mah: there are two types of mawla: one is mawla muwalat – a person who becomes Muslim at someone's hand or makes a pact to stay together for life, they are called mawla muwalat; they do not inherit, but if there is no heir, eventually the property is given to them. The second is the one who frees a slave, called mawla 'itaqah or mawla al-ni'mah; he inherits from the slave. Here mawla al-ni'mah means the manumitter master.

And from the females are seven: (1) the daughter, (2) the son's daughter, (3) the mother, (4) the grandmother, (5) the sister, (6) the wife, (7) the female master of grace (the womanumitress). 
These seven types of women become heirs by consensus, their details will come later. Bint al-ibn: son's daughter, called poti in Urdu. Mawlat al-ni'mah: the woman who freed her slave – the inheritance of that freed slave goes to the mistress; she is called mawlat al-ni'mah or mawlat al-'itaqah. The proof for each will come later.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage is a memorization anchor listing the heirs who inherit by consensus (ijma). The Hanafi madhhab identifies ten male heirs and seven female heirs from the 'asabah and Quranic share holders. The list includes the primary heirs (son, daughter, father, mother, husband, wife) as well as secondary heirs (grandchildren, grandparents, siblings, etc.). The Urdu commentary clarifies important nuances: (1) Ibn al-ibn includes all male descendants through sons, regardless of depth, as long as the line is through males. (2) Al-jadd specifically means paternal grandfather, not maternal grandfather, because maternal grandfather is from dhawi al-arham (distant relatives) who only inherit when no closer heirs exist. (3) Mawla al-ni'mah refers to the manumitter (master) who inherits from a freed slave; this is a unique category of inheritance by virtue of wala' (patronage). The female list similarly includes the female equivalents: daughter, son's daughter, mother, grandmother (paternal or maternal?), sister, wife, and female master. The commentary notes that details and proofs for each will follow later in the text.

Key Terms
مولى النعمة (mawla al-ni'mah): The master who freed a slave; he inherits from the freed slave by virtue of wala'.
ابن الابن (ibn al-ibn): The son's son (grandson) through male line; inherits as asabah.
الجد (al-jadd): Here specifically the paternal grandfather (father's father), not maternal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The seventeen consensus heirs are the foundation of faraid; knowing them is essential for all inheritance calculations.

The Four Legal Impediments to Inheritance in Hanafi Law
Lists four categories excluded from inheritance with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of people who do not inherit in Hanafi law and explain the proofs for each impediment, particularly for slavery and murder.

Core Idea
Four impediments—slavery, murder, apostasy, and difference of religion—completely block inheritance in Hanafi law.

Inheritance in Islamic law is not automatic; certain conditions and impediments (mawani') prevent an otherwise eligible heir from receiving a share. This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri outlines the four key impediments recognized in the Hanafi school and provides textual proofs. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying inheritance rules in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the opening sentence to list the four types of people who do not inherit: slave, murderer, apostate, and person of a different religion.
The Arabic terms: الغلام (al-ghulam) meaning slave, القاتل (al-qatil) meaning murderer, المرند (al-murtadd) meaning apostate, and مختلف الدين (mukhtalif al-din) meaning different religion.
2
Examine the proof for slavery
The passage provides three proofs: rational (the slave's property belongs to the master), hadith (from Bukhari and Muslim about sale of a slave with property), and athar (from Ali ibn Abi Talib that slaves neither prevent nor inherit).
The rational proof is that if a slave inherits, the wealth immediately becomes the master's property.
3
Analyze the proof for murder
The passage gives a rational reason (deterrence) and mentions a hadith fragment: 'the murderer does not inherit'. Note that the hadith is incomplete in the passage.
The Hanafi position is that any unlawful killing prevents inheritance, even accidental.
4
Understand apostasy and difference of religion
These two are listed but not proven in this passage. Their proofs are established elsewhere: apostasy based on the principle that property of an apostate goes to the treasury, and difference of religion based on the hadith 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor a disbeliever from a Muslim.'
The passage focuses on proofs for slavery and murder; apostasy and religion difference are stated without proof here.
5
Summarize the legal effect
Each impediment completely excludes the person from inheritance from the deceased they are related to. For example, a slave cannot inherit from anyone, and no one inherits from a slave (unless freed).
The impediment is total: it prevents both inheriting from and being inherited from.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۲۰۱) (۳) اور چار آدمی وارث نہیں ہوتے (۱) غلام (۲) قاتل مقتول کا (۳) مرند (۴) مختلف دین والے۔ یہ چار قسم کے آدمی وارث نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ ایک تو غلام کسی کا وارث نہیں ہوتا۔ اور وہ خود مر جائے تو اس کا سارا مال آقا کا ہوتا ہے اس لئے کسی اور کو کچھ نہیں ملتا۔ (۱) غلام کسی کا وارث بنے گا تو جیسے ہی اس کے ہاتھ میں مال آئے گا وہ آقا کا ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے وہ خود وارث بنا بھی نہیں بلکہ اس کا آقا وارث بن گیا جو میت کا کوئی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے وہ کسی کا وارث نہیں بنے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ غلام کا مال بائع کا ہوگا یا مشتری کا ہوگا۔ عن سالم بن عبد الله عن ابيه قال سمعت رسول الله الله الله يقول ... ومن ابتاع عبدا وله مال فماله للذي باعه الا ان يشترط المبتاع (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الرجل يكون له ممر او شرب في حائط اونی نخل ، ص ۳۲۰ نمبر ۲۳۷۹ مسلم شریف باب من باع نخلا عليها تمر، ج ۲، ص ۱۰، نمبر ۳۹۰۵/۱۵۴۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام کا مال یا بائع کا ہوگا یا مشتری کا۔ اس لئے وہ وارث نہیں ہوگا (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ ان علیا کسان يقول فى المملوكين واهل الكتاب لا يحجبون ولا يورثون (ب) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۳۳۰ فی الملوک واصل الكتاب من قال لا جون ولا يورثون ، ج سادس ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۳۱۱۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام کسی کا وارث نہیں بنے گا۔ اور جو مال ہے وہ سب آقا کا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کا بھی کوئی وارث نہیں بنے گا۔ ہاں وہ آزاد ہو جائے پھر مرے تو اس کے وارث ہوں گے۔
(۲) قاتل مقتول کا وارث نہیں ہوگا۔ اس نے قتل کر کے مقتول کا مال جلدی حاصل کرنا چاہا تو شریعت نے اس کو وراثت سے ہی محروم کر دیا۔ تا کہ وراثت کے لئے کوئی کسی کو قتل نہ کرے اور جرم زیادہ نہ ہو (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ قاتل وارث نہیں بنے گا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عـن عـمـر بـن شعيب عن ابيه عن
(3201) (3) And four persons do not inherit: (1) the slave, (2) the murderer of the slain person, (3) the apostate, (4) the one of a different religion. These four types of persons do not inherit. Firstly, a slave does not inherit from anyone. And if he dies himself, all his property belongs to his master, so no one else gets anything. (1) If a slave would inherit from someone, as soon as wealth comes into his hand, it becomes the master's property. Therefore he does not become an heir himself; rather his master becomes the heir, who is not related to the deceased. So he does not inherit from anyone. (2) In a hadith: the property of a slave belongs to the seller or the buyer. From Salim ibn Abdullah from his father who said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever buys a slave who has property, his property belongs to the one who sold him, unless the buyer stipulates otherwise.' (a) (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is known that the slave's property belongs either to the seller or the buyer. Therefore he does not inherit. (3) There is an athar: 'Ali used to say regarding slaves and the People of the Book: they neither prevent (others from inheritance) nor do they inherit.' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). From this athar it is known that a slave does not inherit from anyone. And whatever property he has, all belongs to his master. Therefore no one inherits from him either. However, if he becomes free and then dies, then there will be heirs for him.
(2) The murderer will not inherit from the slain. Because he wanted to obtain the property of the slain quickly through killing, so the Shari'ah has deprived him of inheritance entirely, so that no one might kill another for inheritance and crime increase. (2) There is a hadith that the murderer does not inherit. The fragment of the hadith is: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from ...
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage lists the four major legal impediments (mawani') to inheritance in Hanafi law: 1) Slavery (riqq), 2) Homicide (qatl), 3) Apostasy (riddah), and 4) Difference of religion (ikhtilaf al-din). The text then provides detailed proofs for the first impediment (slavery) and begins the proof for the second (murder). For slavery, three proofs are adduced: (a) rational: a slave's acquisitions belong to his master, so he cannot be an heir; (b) hadith from Bukhari and Muslim regarding the sale of a slave with property; (c) athar from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib that slaves and People of the Book neither prevent inheritance nor inherit. This establishes that a slave is completely excluded from inheritance both as an heir and as a testator. However, if the slave is freed, he becomes a full legal subject and his heirs inherit normally. For murder, the text gives a rational reason (deterrence) and mentions a hadith but the text cuts off before the complete citation. The remaining impediments (apostasy and different religion) are listed but not proven in this passage; they will be elaborated later.

Key Terms
القاتل (al-qatil): The person who kills another; prevented from inheriting from the victim.
المرند (al-murtadd): The apostate; a Muslim who renounces Islam; he does not inherit from Muslims and Muslims do not inherit from him.
مختلف الدين (mukhtalif al-din): One of a different religion; a non-Muslim does not inherit from a Muslim, nor vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four impediments to inheritance listed in the passage?
A) Slavery
B) Murder
C) Apostasy
D) Illegitimate birth

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance law, four legal impediments—slavery, murder, apostasy, and difference of religion—completely exclude a person from inheriting from the deceased.

Enumeration of Male and Female Heirs in Hanafi Fara'id
Enumeration of male and female heirs in Hanafi fara'id

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the nine male heirs and seven female heirs recognized in Hanafi inheritance law and identify the basis for their inclusion (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma).

Core Idea
Hanafi inheritance recognizes 16 specific heirs: 9 male and 7 female, including through wala' (freed slave relationship).

This lesson introduces the foundational enumeration of heirs in Hanafi fara'id. Knowing who the legal heirs are is the first step in any inheritance calculation. The passage lists the nine male and seven female heirs, noting that there is consensus (ijma) on the female heirs, and defines two key terms: mawla al-ni'mah (male master) and mawlat al-ni'mah (female master).

Guided Path
1
List the male heirs
Identify the nine male heirs: the husband and the master of the favor (mawla al-ni'mah) are explicitly mentioned. Note that the passage here adds two male heirs (9 and 10) to a previous list (hence the numbers 9 and 10). The full list of nine male heirs is typically: son, grandson (son's son), father, grandfather, brother, nephew, uncle, husband, and mawla al-ni'mah. However, this passage only highlights the husband and mawla. Understand that the term 'mawla al-ni'mah' means the master who freed a slave.
The passage seems to continue a prior enumeration; focus on the two explicitly mentioned.
2
List the female heirs
Identify the seven female heirs: daughter, son's daughter (bint al-ibn), mother, grandmother (jaddah), sister, wife, and female master of the favor (mawlat al-ni'mah). The passage states there is consensus (ijma) on these seven.
Grandmother here includes both paternal and maternal grandmothers.
3
Define key terms: mawla al-ni'mah and mawlat al-ni'mah
Understand that mawla al-ni'mah is the male master who frees a slave; he inherits from the freed slave. Similarly, mawlat al-ni'mah is the female master who frees a female slave. This is inheritance through wala' (clientage).
Wala' is a cause of inheritance separate from blood relations.
4
Recognize the consensus and subsequent details
The passage notes that the details of each heir will follow later. For now, commit the eight categories (seven female + husband + mawla) to memory.
The numbers in parentheses (e.g., (1), (2)) are likely from the original text.

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Inheritance (Kitab al-Fara'id) by listing the male and female heirs. The text enumerates nine male heirs and seven female heirs. The male heirs include the husband and the master of the favor (mawla al-ni'mah), while the female heirs include the daughter, son's daughter, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and female master of the favor. The commentary explains that the term 'mawla al-ni'mah' refers to the master who has freed a slave; such a master inherits from the freed slave. The female counterpart is 'mawlat al-ni'mah' or 'mawlat al-'itaqah'. The passage notes that on these seven female heirs there is consensus (ijma'), and the details of each will be given later. This is a foundational enumeration in Hanafi inheritance law, establishing the categories of legal heirs.

Key Terms
مولى النعمة (mawla al-ni'mah): The master who frees a slave; he inherits from the freed slave.
بنت الابن (bint al-ibn): The son's daughter (granddaughter through a son).
مولاۃ النعمہ (mawlat al-ni'mah): The female master who frees a female slave; she inherits from the freed slave.

Faraid — Inheritance

Four Categories Excluded from Inheritance
Detailing the four categories excluded from inheritance with textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of people excluded from inheritance in Hanafi faraid and identify the textual proofs for each.

Core Idea
Four types are permanently barred: slave, killer, apostate, and those of different religions.

This passage from a Hanafi faraid text outlines four categories of individuals who are disqualified from inheriting. Each category is supported by explicit textual evidence from the Quran, Hadith, or Athar. Understanding these exclusions is essential for correctly applying inheritance law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Read the passage to name the four categories of people who do not inherit: slave, killer, apostate, and people of different religions.
These are permanent exclusions unless the person's status changes (e.g., slave freed, apostate returns to Islam).
2
Locate the textual proof for each
For each category, note the specific proof cited: hadith for killer and religious difference, verse for apostate, athar for slave.
The proofs are from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Understand the rationale
Understand why each exclusion exists: slave lacks property ownership, killer is deterred, apostate's deeds are void, religious difference prevents mutual inheritance.
The rationale is rooted in preserving the integrity of inheritance and preventing abuse.
4
Apply the rule
When analyzing a real inheritance case, check if any heir falls into these categories. If so, that heir receives nothing.
Freedom, repentance, or conversion can remove the bar, but timing matters (status at time of death).

And no one inherits? Here 'master of the favor' means the master who freed. (3201) (3) And four persons do not inherit: (1) a slave, (2) the killer of the slain person, (3) an apostate, (4) those of different religions. These four types of people do not inherit. First, a slave does not inherit from anyone. And if he dies, all his wealth belongs to his master, so no one else gets anything. (1) If a slave were to inherit, as soon as property comes into his hand, it becomes the master's. So he does not actually become an heir; rather, his master becomes the heir, who is not connected to the deceased. Therefore, he does not inherit from anyone. (2) The hadith: the property of a slave belongs to the seller or the buyer. From Salim ibn Abdullah from his father: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever buys a slave who has property, his property belongs to the one who sold him, unless the buyer stipulates [otherwise].' (Bukhari and Muslim) This hadith shows that the slave's property belongs to either the seller or the buyer, so he does not inherit. (3) The athar: Ali used to say concerning slaves and the People of the Book: they do not veil (others) nor are they inherited. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This shows that a slave does not inherit from anyone, and whatever property he has belongs to his master. So no one inherits from him either. However, if he is freed and then dies, he will have heirs. (2) The killer does not inherit from the slain person. He wanted to hasten acquisition of the slain person's property through killing, so the Shariah deprived him of inheritance, so that no one kills another for inheritance and crime does not increase. (2) The hadith: the killer does not inherit. The segment: From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from [the four: slave, killer of the slain, apostate, and people of two religions? Actually the hadith text is: 'There is nothing for the killer. And if he has no heir, then his nearest relative inherits from him, and the killer does not inherit anything.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that the killer does not inherit. The apostate does not inherit. He will be executed, so how can he inherit? (2) Indication of non-inheritance is in the verse: 'And whoever among you apostatizes from his religion and dies while a disbeliever – those have wasted their deeds in this world and the Hereafter.' (2:217) In this verse, the deeds of the apostate are ruined in both worlds. So from the ruin in this world is that he is deprived of inheritance. (3) Moreover, he has become a disbeliever, and how can a disbeliever inherit from a Muslim? (4) The athar: Ali was brought Mustawrid al-'Ijli who had apostatized; he presented Islam to him, but he refused, so Ali killed him and made his inheritance among his Muslim heirs. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This shows that a male apostate is killed, so he does not inherit from anyone. If female, she is imprisoned until she repents, so she also does not inherit. And people of two different religions do not inherit from each other. The hadith: A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor a disbeliever from a Muslim. (Bukhari, Muslim) From Usamah ibn Zayd that the Prophet said: 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor a disbeliever from a Muslim.' This shows that a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever and a disbeliever does not inherit from a Muslim. (2) Another hadith: From Jabir from the Prophet: 'People of two different religions do not inherit from each other.' (Tirmidhi) This hadith says that two people of different religions do not inherit from each other.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage discusses the four categories of people who are permanently barred from inheriting in Islamic law: slaves, killers, apostates, and people of different religions. Each category is supported by textual evidence. For slaves, the commentary explains that a slave cannot own property independently; everything he acquires belongs to his master. Therefore, he cannot inherit because if he did, the property would immediately transfer to his master, who is not a legal heir of the deceased. The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about buying a slave with property reinforces that the slave's property is tied to his master. The athar from Ali further confirms that slaves neither block others from inheriting nor are they considered heirs. For killers, the rationale is to prevent killing for inheritance; the hadith explicitly states that a killer has no share. For apostates, the verse from Surah Al-Baqarah (2:217) indicates that their deeds are nullified, and the athar from Ali shows that a male apostate is executed and his property goes to his Muslim heirs. For religious difference, the hadiths establish that Muslims and disbelievers do not inherit from each other, and followers of two different religions cannot inherit from each other. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi inheritance law, with the exception that if a Muslim inherits from a non-Muslim? Actually Hanafi law does not allow mutual inheritance across religions. The commentary also notes that if a slave is freed, he becomes eligible to inherit and be inherited from.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A slave; he is barred from inheriting because his property belongs to his master.
قاتل (qatil): The killer of the deceased; he is deprived of inheritance as a deterrent.
مرتد (murtadd): A person who leaves Islam; he does not inherit from Muslims and his property goes to Muslim heirs.
أهل الملتين (ahl al-millatayn): People of two different religions; they do not inherit from each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A son who disobeys his father

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, four categories of people are permanently excluded from inheritance: slaves, killers, apostates, and those of different religions.

Faraid — Inheritance

The Six Fixed Shares (Furud) in Qur'anic Inheritance
Enumerating the six prescribed fractional shares mentioned in the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six fixed shares and identify which heirs are entitled to each share.

Core Idea
The Quran defines six fractional shares—half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, one-third, one-sixth—that certain heirs receive under specific conditions.

In Islamic inheritance, the Quran specifies six fixed fractions (furud) that certain heirs are entitled to. These fractions form the foundation of faraid calculations. This lesson will introduce each share and the heirs who may receive it, anchoring your knowledge of these divine ordinances.

Guided Path
1
List the six shares
Write down the six fractions: half (1/2), quarter (1/4), eighth (1/8), two-thirds (2/3), one-third (1/3), and one-sixth (1/6). Memorize them in order.
These are the only fractional shares expressly mentioned in the Quran for inheritance.
2
Identify the heir(s) for each share
For each share, recall which heir(s) may receive it and under what condition. For example, half goes to a husband if the deceased has no child, or to a daughter if she is the only child.
Use the key terms in this lesson for reference.
3
Recognize that shares are conditional
Note that the same heir may receive a different share depending on the presence of other heirs. For instance, a mother receives 1/3 if no children but 1/6 if children exist.
The conditions are derived from the Quranic verses of inheritance.
4
Distinguish fixed shares from residuary inheritance
Understand that not all heirs inherit by fixed shares; some inherit as residuaries (asabah) who take the remainder after fixed shares are distributed.
This distinction is crucial for calculating actual portions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۰۲) (۴) وہ حصے جو کتاب اللہ میں مقرر ہیں وہ چھ ہیں (۱) آدھا (۲) چوتھائی (۳) آٹھواں (۴) دو تہائی (۵) ایک تہائی (۶) چھٹا۔ پچھلے زمانے میں کھلیکیولیٹر نہیں تھا اس لئے لوگ کسر سے حساب نہیں کرتے تھے بلکہ اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دے کر صحیح عدد نکالتے تھے۔ لیکن ابھی کلکولیٹر کی سہولت ہے اس لئے اس کا حساب لکھا جائے گا۔ چونکہ کلکولیٹر ہمیشہ سو سے حساب بناتا ہے اس لئے ہمیشہ اصل مسئلہ سو سے
[3202] (4) The shares that are appointed in the Book of Allah are six: (1) half, (2) quarter, (3) eighth, (4) two-thirds, (5) one-third, (6) one-sixth. In earlier times there was no calculator, so people would not calculate fractions; rather, they would multiply the base problem to get a whole number. But now there is the convenience of a calculator, so its calculation will be written. Since a calculator always computes from a hundred, we will always set the base problem from a hundred.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage enumerates the six fixed shares (furud) mentioned in the Quran for inheritance. They are half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, one-third, and one-sixth. These are the fractional shares that certain heirs receive under specific conditions. The commentary then notes a methodological point: in the past, without calculators, scholars used to multiply the base number of the inheritance problem to avoid fractions. Now with calculators, it is easier to compute using a base of 100. This reflects an adaptation to modern tools while retaining the classical system. The explanation suggests that the author or commentator prefers using 100 as the base for calculations instead of the traditional base numbers (like 6, 12, 24, etc.) for convenience.

Key Terms
آدھا (aadha): Half (1/2), a fixed share for certain heirs like husband, daughter, sister, etc.
چوتھائی (chouthaai): Quarter (1/4), e.g., husband inherits quarter if spouse has no child, wife inherits quarter if no child.
آٹھواں (aathwan): Eighth (1/8), the share of a wife when the deceased has children.
دو تہائی (do tehai): Two-thirds (2/3), e.g., two or more daughters collectively, or two or more sisters.
ایک تہائی (ek tehai): One-third (1/3), e.g., mother's share when no children, or two or more siblings of mother.
چھٹا (chhata): One-sixth (1/6), e.g., mother when there are children, or siblings of mother alone, or son's daughter, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six fixed shares in Quranic inheritance?
A) Half
B) One-third
C) Fifth
D) Eighth

Key Takeaway
The six fixed shares are half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, one-third, and one-sixth; each applies to specific heirs under specified conditions.

Faraid — Inheritance

The Four Categories of Non-Heirs in Hanafi Faraid
Lists and proves the four who are prevented from inheriting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four categories of persons prevented from inheriting in Hanafi law and state the primary evidence (dalil) for each category.

Core Idea
Four types of persons can never inherit: a slave, the killer of the deceased, an apostate, and a non-Muslim relative of a Muslim.

In the Hanafi school of inheritance (faraid), not every relative is entitled to inherit. Certain individuals are permanently barred due to their status or actions. This lesson presents the four categories of such non-heirs, grounding each ruling in primary texts from the Quran, Sunnah, and the practice of the Companions. Understanding these bars is essential for correctly distributing an estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Categories
Read the opening sentence of the passage. It lists four categories: the slave, the killer of the deceased, the apostate, and the people of two different religions (i.e., Muslim and non-Muslim). Commit these to memory as the 'four permanent bars'.
These are not the only bars; there are also partial bars (hajb nuqsan), but these are absolute exclusions.
2
Find the Proof for Each Category
The passage provides a proof for three of the four categories. Locate the hadith for the killer (no inheritance for the killer), the Quranic verse and athar for the apostate, and the hadith for people of different religions. The slave is mentioned without proof in this passage; it is a well-known ruling based on the slave's lack of legal capacity.
The proofs are from primary sources: Quran (2:217), Hadith (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi), and Athar (Ali).
3
Understand the Rationale (Wajh al-Dalalah)
For the killer, the hadith 'the killer has nothing' is general and covers all types of killing, even accidental. For the apostate, the verse nullifies all deeds, including inheritance rights; additionally, the male apostate is executed, making inheritance impossible. For different religions, the hadith explicitly negates mutual inheritance.
The Hanafi school takes these proofs as absolute bars; no exceptions are made for accidental killing or close non-Muslim relatives.
4
Recognise the Practical Effect
When computing shares in an estate, the first step is to identify all surviving relatives, then exclude those who fall into one of these four categories. For example, a non-Muslim spouse does not inherit from a Muslim deceased, and a child who kills their parent is excluded entirely.
These bars apply regardless of the degree of relationship.

Four: the slave, the killer of the slain, the apostate, and the people of two religions. [3202 (3) And the fixed shares... He said: The Messenger of Allah said... And the Messenger of Allah said: There is nothing for the killer, and if he has no heir, then his nearest relative is his heir, and the killer does not inherit anything. From this hadith it is understood that the killer will not inherit. The apostate will not inherit. He will be killed, so how can he inherit? (2) Indication of not inheriting is in this verse: 'And whoever of you turns back from his religion and dies while he is a disbeliever – then those have nullified their deeds in this world and the Hereafter.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:217) In this verse, the deeds of the apostate are ruined in both worlds. So from worldly ruin, he will be deprived of inheritance. (3) Also, he became a disbeliever, and how can a disbeliever inherit from a Muslim? (4) There is an athar: 'From Ali that Mastawrid al-'Ijli was brought to him, and he had apostatized. He presented Islam to him, but he refused, so he killed him and made his inheritance between his Muslim heirs.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this athar it is understood that if a male apostatizes, he will be killed, so he will not inherit from anyone. If it is a female, she will be imprisoned until she repents, so she also will not inherit. And the people of two religions will not inherit from each other. In a hadith: The disbeliever does not inherit from the Muslim, nor the Muslim from the disbeliever. From Usama bin Zaid that the Prophet said: 'The Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever, nor the disbeliever from the Muslim.' (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith it is understood that the Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever and the disbeliever does not inherit from the Muslim. (2) In another hadith: From Jabir from the Prophet said: 'The people of two religions do not inherit from each other.' (Tirmidhi) In this hadith, followers of two different religions will not inherit from each other.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samarqandi states a key legal principle in the Hanafi inheritance system: the four categories of people who are entirely prevented from inheriting (mamnu'un min al-irth). 1) The slave (mamluk): a slave cannot inherit because they themselves are owned property. 2) The killer (qatil): one who causes the death of the deceased is barred from inheriting, based on the hadith 'the killer has nothing.' This applies to intentional and unjustified killing. 3) The apostate (murtadd): a person who leaves Islam. For males, the punishment is execution, so they cannot inherit; for females, they are imprisoned, and also cannot inherit because of difference of religion. The Quranic verse (2:217) is cited to show that the apostate's deeds are nullified, including inheritance rights. 4) People of different religions (ahl al-millatayn): a Muslim and a non-Muslim cannot inherit from each other, based on the famous hadith. The Hanafi school holds this as a complete bar: a disbeliever never inherits from a Muslim, and vice versa. The proofs are all from primary sources: Quran, Sunnah, and the practice of the Companions (athar from Ali). The author presents these as settled rulings.

Key Terms
القاتل (al-qatil): The killer who directly causes the death of the deceased, whether intentional or accidental.
المرتد (al-murtadd): A Muslim who leaves Islam and does not return.
أهل الملتين (ahl al-millatayn): Followers of two different religions, specifically Muslim and non-Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The killer (qatil)
C) The orphan (yatim)
D) The apostate (murtadd)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance law, four categories of persons are permanently barred from inheriting: the slave, the killer, the apostate, and those of a different religion from the deceased.

The Six Fixed Shares in Faraid (Percentage Calculation)
Enumeration of six fixed shares and their percentage equivalents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six fixed fractional shares in Faraid and convert each to its percentage equivalent using a base of 100.

Core Idea
Six Quranic shares — half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, sixth — each converts to a fixed percentage.

This lesson presents the six mandatory fractional shares that form the foundation of inheritance distribution. You will not only memorize them but also learn a modern method to express them as percentages using 100 as the base, making calculation straightforward with a calculator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six shares
Memorize the names and fractions: nisf (½), rub' (¼), thumn (⅛), thuluthan (⅔), thuluth (⅓), sudus (⅙).
These are the only fractional shares mentioned in the Quran for inheritance.
2
Understand the base-100 method
Treat the total estate as 100 units (or 100%) for convenience. This avoids working with multiple denominators.
Classical scholars used integer fractions; calculators allow percentage breakdown.
3
Calculate each share as a percentage
Divide 100 by the denominator: half = 50, quarter = 25, eighth = 12.5, two-thirds = 66.66..., third = 33.33..., sixth = 16.66...
Repeating decimals (66.66, 33.33, 16.66) are rounded; exact values are irrational.
4
Recognize the fixed nature
These percentages are derived from Qur'anic verses and are immutable in fiqh.
No ijtihad can change the shares; they are tawqifi (divinely prescribed).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The fixed shares in the Book of Allah Almighty are six: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth. The shares that are determined in the Book of Allah are six: 1) half, 2) quarter, 3) eighth, 4) two-thirds, 5) one-third, 6) sixth. In earlier times there was no calculator, so people would not calculate with fractions, but would multiply the base problem to get a correct integer. But now with the convenience of the calculator, its calculation will be written. Since the calculator always calculates from one hundred, the base problem will always be from one hundred, neither less nor more. Also, in calculation decimal will be used, which in English is called point. For example, to write two and a half, write 2.5 – two point five, which in Urdu is 'do ashariya panch'. And the number that comes after the point is a tenth of one number. Now the calculation of shares will be like this: half of one hundred is fifty, quarter of one hundred is twenty-five, eighth of one hundred is twelve and a half (12.5), two-thirds of one hundred is sixty-six point six-six (66.66), one-third of one hundred is thirty-three point three-three (33.33), and sixth of one hundred is sixteen point six-six (16.66). Look at its detail at a glance.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage states a foundational listing in Hanafi inheritance law: the six fractional shares (furud muqaddara) that are explicitly mentioned in the Quran. The six are: nisf (1/2), rub' (1/4), thumn (1/8), thuluthan (2/3), thuluth (1/3), and sudus (1/6). These are the only possible fractional shares that heirs receive from the estate. The author then provides a modern method using percentages (out of 100) and decimal points to aid calculation. He explains that earlier scholars would find a common denominator (asl al-mas'ala) and use integer fractions, but calculators allow easy conversion to percentages. So for convenience, he teaches to take the base as 100. For example, half of 100 is 50, quarter is 25, etc. This is a pedagogical tool, not a change in the fiqh ruling. The shares themselves are fixed by divine text.

Key Terms
النصف (an-nisf): One half of the estate.
الربع (ar-rub'): One quarter of the estate.
الثمن (ath-thumn): One eighth of the estate.
الثلثان (ath-thuluthan): Two-thirds of the estate.
الثلث (ath-thuluth): One third of the estate.
السدس (as-sudus): One sixth of the estate.

Key Takeaway
The six fixed shares are half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth; they can be expressed as percentages for modern calculation but their fiqh basis remains unchanged.

Heirs Entitled to Half Share (Nisf) – Part One
Lists half-share heirs and gives Quranic proof for daughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five heirs entitled to half share in Hanafi faraid and state the condition for each from the text.

Core Idea
Half share is a fixed Quranic right for five specific heirs when no higher or equal heir blocks them to a lesser share.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the half share (nisf) is one of six fixed shares prescribed by the Quran. This passage introduces five categories of heirs who may receive half under specific conditions, beginning with the solitary daughter and her clear proof from Surah an-Nisa. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct inheritance distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that half is the share of five specific types of heirs. Recognize that this is a fixed share (fard) contingent on conditions.
2
List the five heirs and their conditions
Extract from the text: (1) daughter when no son, (2) granddaughter when no direct daughter, (3) full sister (condition not fully stated here), (4) consanguine sister when no full sister, (5) husband when no descendants.
The conditions for full sister and husband appear elsewhere; focus on what the text provides.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof for the daughter
The author cites Quran 4:11: 'if there is only one daughter, for her is half.' Note the explicit text (qat'i dalalah) and how it establishes the daughter's half share directly.
Hanafi usul: the imperative and explicit phrase yield a binding ruling.
4
Examine the incomplete hadith reference
The passage begins a hadith about Mu'adh's judgment, but it is cut off. Understand that this hadith is supplementary evidence for the daughter's half, though the Quran is primary.
The hadith may also address when the daughter inherits along with a sister; full narration is beyond this chunk.
5
Apply the ruling to a simple scenario
Example: A man dies leaving one daughter and no son. She inherits half. Confirm that no other condition (e.g., presence of spouse or parents) reduces or changes her share here, though other heirs may affect distribution.
This lesson focuses on the half entitlement; full distribution involves other shares.

In the verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male the equivalent of the share of two females. Commentary
This passage begins a detailed discussion of the 'half' (nisf) share in Hanafi inheritance law. It first lists five heirs who are entitled to receive half the estate under specific conditions: 1) the daughter (bint) when she is alone (no son, no other daughter to make two-thirds), 2) the granddaughter (bint al-ibn) when there is no son's daughter? Actually 'when there is no son's daughter' is ambiguous: the condition is that there is no other female descendant at a higher level? The text says 'جبکہ مصلبی بیٹی نہ ہو' meaning 'when there is no direct daughter' i.e., the granddaughter only gets half if there is no daughter from the son? Actually careful: 'مصلبی بیٹی' means 'daughter of the son'? No, 'مصلبی' likely 'صُلبی' meaning 'direct' (own daughter). So condition: when there is no direct daughter. Then 3) full sister (ukht sha'ira), 4) consanguine sister (ukht min al-ab) when full sister is absent, 5) husband in the absence of any descendant (child or grandchild). Then the author begins explaining the first case: the solitary daughter. He cites Quran 4:11 which explicitly gives half to the single daughter. He also starts citing a hadith about Mu'adh's judgment. The passage is cut off, but the lesson introduces the list of half-share heirs. The Hanafi school follows these categories based on the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
النصف (an-nisf): The half share of the estate, one of the six fixed shares.
البنت (al-bint): The daughter of the deceased.
بنت الابن (bint al-ibn): The granddaughter from the son.
صُلبیہ (sulbiyyah): Direct daughter (from the deceased's loins), as opposed to granddaughter.
حقیقی بہن (haqiqi bahan): Full sister (same mother and father).
باپ شریک بہن (baap shareek bahan): Consanguine sister (same father, different mother).

The Half Share and Its Five Recipients
Ruling with proof on half share recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five heirs who receive the half share and identify the conditions under which each qualifies.

Core Idea
Half the inheritance goes to one of five specific heirs, but only when no closer heir blocks them.

This passage from the Hanafi faraid tradition introduces the half share (al-nisf) as one of six fixed Quranic shares. It then lists five categories of heirs who are entitled to half, each with a clear condition that must be met. We will examine each category, the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and the rules of exclusion (hajb) that apply. Understanding these foundational categories is essential before moving to more complex inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five half-share recipients
Read the list: daughter, granddaughter (son's daughter), full sister, paternal half-sister, and husband. Note the conditions: each receives half only when certain other heirs are absent.
2
Analyze the condition for each recipient
For the daughter: must be only one and no son. For the granddaughter: no direct daughter. For full sister: no daughter, no son, no granddaughter. For half-sister: no full sister. For husband: no child or grandchild of the deceased.
These conditions are applications of hajb (exclusion/reduction).
3
Examine the textual proofs
The passage cites Quran 4:11 for the daughter, a hadith from Mu'adh for the full sister, an athar from Ibn Thabit for the granddaughter's substitution, and a hadith from Abu Musa for the granddaughter's share when a daughter is present.
The proofs are dalil naqli (textual evidence) and are used to establish the rules.
4
Understand the rule for granddaughter with daughter
When a daughter and granddaughter coexist without a son, the daughter takes half, and the granddaughter takes one-sixth to complete two-thirds, as per the hadith. This prevents the granddaughter from taking half when a daughter is present.
This shows the Hanafi principle that grandchildren substitute for children in absence.
5
Apply the half share rule
Given a scenario, determine who qualifies for half. For example, a deceased leaves only a full sister: she takes half. If a daughter and a full sister exist, the daughter takes half, the sister takes what remains (asabah) or is excluded? Actually the sister would be blocked by the daughter? The passage does not cover that here; but the half share conditions are clear.
This step prepares for practical calculation.

المحدودة فى كتاب الله تعالى ستة النصف والربع والثمن والثلثان والثلث والسدس.
(۵) آدھا پانچ آدمیوں کا حصہ ہے (۱) بیٹی (۲) پوتی جبکہ مصلبی بیٹی نہ ہو (۳) حقیقی بہن (۴) باپ شریک بہن جبکہ حقیقی بہن نہ ہو (۵) شوہر جبکہ میت کی اولاد نہ ہوں اور نہ اولاد کی اولاد ہو چاہے نیچے کا ہو۔
ت ان پانچ آدمیوں کو آدھا ملتا ہے۔ کس حالت میں آدھا ملے گا اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔
(۱) اگر صرف ایک بیٹی ہو اور بیٹا نہ ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔
آیت میں ہے۔ یوصيكم الله فى اولادكم للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين فان كن نساء فوق اثنتين فلهن ثلاثا ماترک وان كانت واحدة فلها النصف (الف) ( آيت اا، سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بیٹا نہ ہو اور ایک بیٹی ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ قال اتانا معاذ بن جبل باليمن معلما واميرا فسألناه عن رجل توفي وترك ابنته واخته فاعطى الابنة النصف والاخت النصف (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث البنات ، ص ۱۹۹۷ نمبر ۶۷۳۴ را بودا و دشریف ، باب ماجاء فی میراث الصلب ، ص ۴۴، نمبر ۲۸۹۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک بیٹی ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔
(۲) اگر صلبی بیٹی موجود نہ ہو اور ایک پوتی ہو تو صلبی بیٹی کی طرح ایک پوتی کو آدھا ملے گا۔ صلبی بیٹی نہ ہونے کی شکل میں پوتی بیٹی کی جگہ پر ہوتی ہے۔ اور جس طرح ایک بیٹی کو آدھا ملتا ہے اسی طرح پوتی کو بھی آدھا ملے گا (۱) اثر میں ہے کہ صلبی بیٹا نہ ہوتو پوتا اس کی جگہ پر اتناہی کا حصہ دار ہوتا ہے اسی طرح صلبی بیٹی نہ ہو تو پوتی اس کی جگہ اتنے ہی کا حصہ دار بنتی ہے۔ اس لئے ایک پوتی ہو تو ایک بیٹی کی طرح اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔ اثر یہ ہے۔ قال ابن ثابت ولد الابناء بمنزلة الولد اذا لم يكن دونهم ولد ذكر، ذكرهم كذكرهم وانثاهم كانثاهم، يرثون كما يرثون ويحجبون كما يحجبون ،ولا يرث ولد الابن مع الابن (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث ابن الابن اذا لم یکن ابن ہی ۹۹۷، نمبر ۶۷۳۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مصلبی اولاد نہ ہو تو ایک پوتی ایک بیٹی کی جگہ پر ہو کر آدھا ملے گا (۲) پوتی کی اتنی اہمیت ہے کہ ایک بیٹی ہو اور ایک ہوتی ہوتو دو تہائی مکمل کرنے کے لئے بیٹی کو آدھا اور پوتی کو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا تا کہ دو بیٹی کی طرح دو تہائی مکمل ہو جائے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ مسئل ابو موسى عن ابنة وابنة ابن واخت ... اقضى فيها بما قضى النبي الا الله لابنة النصف ولابنة الابن السدس تكملة الثلثين ومابقی فللاخت (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث ابنته ابن مع ابته، ص ۹۹۷، نمبر ۶۷۳۶ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی میراث بنت الابن مع بنت الصلب ، ج ۲، ص ۲۹، نمبر ۲۰۹۳) اس حدیث میں پوتی کی اتنی اہمیت ہے کہ دوسری بیٹی نہ ہونے پر دو ٹکٹ پورا کرنے کے لئے پوتی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا۔ اس لئے بیٹی نہ ہونے پر پوتی کو ملے گا۔
(۳) ماں باپ شریک بہن یعنی بیٹی بھی نہیں ہے اور بیٹا بھی نہیں ہے اور پوتی بھی نہیں ہے اور ایک ماں باپ شریک بہن ہے جس کو حقیقی بہن کہتے ہیں تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔
حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ قال اتانا معاذ بن جبل باليمن معلما واميرا فسألناه عن رجل توفی وترک ابنته واخته فاعطی الابنة النصف والاخت النصف (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث البنات ، ص ۹۹۷، نمبر ۶۷۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حقیقی ایک بہن کے لئے آدھا ہے (۲) آیت میں بھی اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ يستفتونك قل الله يفتيكم في الكلالة ان امرؤ هلک لیس له ولد وله اخت فلها نصف ماترك وهو يرثها ان لم يكن لها ولد، فان كانتا اثنتين فلهما الثلثان مماترك وان
The fixed shares in Allah's book are six: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth. (5) Half is the share of five persons: (1) daughter (2) son's daughter (granddaughter) when there is no direct daughter (3) full sister (4) paternal half-sister when there is no full sister (5) husband when the deceased has no children and no grandchildren, even if lower. So these five persons receive half. In what condition do they receive half? The detail is as follows. (1) If there is only one daughter and no son, she receives half. In the verse: 'Allah commands you concerning your children: for the male is the equal of the share of two females. But if there are [only] two or more females, they get two-thirds of what he leaves; and if there is only one, she gets half.' (Surah Nisa 4:11) This verse indicates that if there is no son and one daughter, she receives half. (2) Hadith: Mu'adh ibn Jabal came to us in Yemen as a teacher and governor. We asked him about a man who died leaving a daughter and a sister. He gave the daughter half and the sister half. (Bukhari, Book of Inheritance of Daughters, p.1997, no.6734) From this hadith it is understood that one daughter receives half. (2) If there is no direct daughter and there is one granddaughter (son's daughter), then the granddaughter is like the daughter and receives half. (1) Athar: Ibn Thabit said: The children of sons are like children when there is no child (son) below them. Their males are like their males and their females are like their females. They inherit as they inherit and they prevent as they prevent. And the child of a son does not inherit with a son. (Bukhari, Book of Inheritance of Son's Son, p.997, no.6735) From this athar it is understood that when there is no direct descendant, one granddaughter takes the place of a daughter and receives half. (2) The importance of the granddaughter is such that if there is one daughter and one granddaughter, to complete two-thirds, the daughter takes half and the granddaughter takes one-sixth, so that two-thirds is completed like two daughters. Hadith: Abu Musa was asked about a daughter, a granddaughter, and a sister... He said: I decide as the Prophet (peace be upon him) decided: For the daughter half, for the granddaughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and the rest for the sister. (Bukhari, p.997, no.6736; Tirmidhi, vol.2, p.29, no.2093) In this hadith, the granddaughter's importance is such that when there is no second daughter, she is given one-sixth to complete two-thirds. Therefore, when there is no daughter, the granddaughter takes (half). (3) A full sister (i.e., there is no daughter, no son, no granddaughter, and there is one full sister) receives half. The hadith has passed: Mu'adh ibn Jabal gave the daughter half and the sister half. From this hadith it is understood that one full sister receives half. (2) There is also proof from the verse: 'They request from you a ruling. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning the one who has neither parents nor children: If a man dies leaving no child and he has a sister, she gets half of what he leaves, and he will inherit from her if she leaves no child. But if there are two sisters, they get two-thirds of what he leaves...' (Surah Nisa 4:176).
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school explaining the half share (nisf) in inheritance. It begins by listing the six fixed shares mentioned in the Quran. Then it specifically addresses the half share, stating that five categories of heirs can receive half under certain conditions: daughter, granddaughter (son's daughter) when no direct daughter, full sister, paternal half-sister when no full sister, and husband when the deceased has no children or grandchildren. The author then details each category with Qur'anic verses, hadith, and an athar from Ibn Thabit. For the daughter, Qur'an 4:11 is cited to show that a single daughter receives half. For the granddaughter, an athar of Ibn Thabit establishes that grandchildren stand in place of children when there are no direct children. The hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal is used to prove the half share for a full sister. The passage also notes that when a daughter and granddaughter exist together, the daughter receives half and the granddaughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds, as per the hadith of Abu Musa. This follows the Hanafi principle that grandchildren inherit in place of children when the latter are absent.

Key Terms
النصف (al-nisf): One of six fixed Quranic shares; equal to half of the inheritance.
الصلبية (al-salbiyyah): Direct daughter of the deceased (from his own loins).
حجاب (hajab): Preclusion or reduction of an heir's share due to another heir's existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who receives the half share when the deceased leaves no children or grandchildren, but has a full sister?
A) The full sister receives half.
B) The full sister receives one-third.
C) The full sister receives two-thirds.
D) The full sister receives nothing.

Key Takeaway
The half share is given to five specific heirs only when no closer heir exists, as established by Quran and Sunnah.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
6 min
The Five Heirs Who Inherit Half
Listing and proving five heirs entitled to half share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five heirs entitled to a half share (al-nisf) in Hanafi faraid and state the conditions under which each receives this share.

Core Idea
Five heirs inherit half: daughter, son's daughter, full sister, consanguine sister, husband—each under specific conditions.

This passage from Kitab al-Fara'id systematically lists the five categories of heirs who receive a fixed half share of the estate. For each heir, the author provides textual evidence from the Quran and authentic hadith, and clarifies important subsidiary rulings—such as how a son's daughter inherits alongside a daughter. Understanding these foundational rules is essential for correctly distributing an estate in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
List the five half-share heirs
Identify each of the five heirs mentioned: daughter, son's daughter, full sister, consanguine sister, and husband. Note the specific conditions that trigger the half share for each (e.g., no son for the daughter, no child for the husband).
These are fixed Quranic shares (furuḍ).
2
Examine the evidence for each heir
For each heir, locate the dalil cited: the Quranic verses (4:12 for husband, 4:176 for sister) and the hadith (e.g., Mu'adh's decision for daughter and sister). Understand how the proof establishes the share.
All evidence is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala.
3
Analyze the subsidiary ruling on daughter and son's daughter
When there is one daughter and one son's daughter, the daughter gets half and the son's daughter gets one-sixth to complete two-thirds. This prevents exceeding the Quranic two-thirds limit for two daughters.
This ruling is based on the hadith of Abu Musa.
4
Distinguish full sister from consanguine sister
The full sister (ukht shaqiqah) is the primary heir; the consanguine sister (ukht li-ab) takes her place only when no full sister exists. The verse uses 'sister' generally, but the full sister's precedence is established by hadith.
The consanguine sister's half share is conditional on absence of full sister.
5
Confirm the husband's half share condition
The husband gets half only when the deceased wife has no child (son or daughter). If there is a child, his share reduces to one-fourth. This is explicit in Quran 4:12.
The same rule applies regardless of whether the child is from this husband or a previous marriage.

Source Text
