The one-third share is for every two or more of the children of the mother, males and females among them are equal in it. The explanation: For a single uterine brother or sister, one-sixth. For two or more, one-third, shared equally regardless of gender. Example: if a deceased leaves a uterine brother and a uterine sister, they receive 16.16 each from the one-third, and the remaining two-thirds go to the father as an asabah. The evidence is Quran 4:12 and the narration of Zaid ibn Thabit.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the inheritance share of uterine siblings (children of the mother). It clarifies that when there are two or more uterine siblings, they collectively receive one-third of the estate, and they divide it equally among themselves, irrespective of gender. This is a departure from the general rule of the male receiving twice the female's share and is based on the Quranic verse (An-Nisa 4:12): 'If they are more than one, they share in one-third.' The passage also includes an example calculation where a uterine brother and sister each receive equal shares from the one-third, and the father takes the remaining two-thirds as residuary heir. The commentary cites a narration from Zaid ibn Thabit confirming that uterine siblings do not inherit in the presence of a child or father, and for a single uterine sibling the share is one-sixth.

Key Terms
ولد الام (walad al-umm): Children of the same mother but different fathers (uterine siblings).
السدس (al-suds): The one-sixth share prescribed for certain heirs.
الثلث (al-thuluth): The one-third share for multiple uterine siblings.

Seven Categories of Heirs Receiving One-Sixth Share
Lists seven categories of one-sixth heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven categories of heirs who receive one-sixth in Hanafi faraid and state the Quranic proof for the parent's share.

Core Idea
Seven heirs receive one-sixth; each share is conditional upon other heirs being present.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the one-sixth share (suds) is a fixed Quranic share assigned to specific heirs under precise conditions. This passage enumerates seven categories, each with its own qualifying circumstances, supported by Quranic verses and narrations from Zaid ibn Thabit. Understanding these categories is foundational to calculating inheritance correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven categories
Read the list and note each category: (1) each parent with child/grandchild, (2) mother with siblings, (3) grandmother, (4) grandfather with child/grandchild, (5) granddaughters with one daughter, (6) consanguine sisters with one full sister, (7) one uterine sibling.
These are the only heirs who can receive one-sixth under specific conditions.
2
Draw the conditions for each category
For each category, determine what condition must be present (e.g., parent gets one-sixth only if there is a child or grandchild; mother gets one-sixth if there are multiple siblings).
Without the condition, the share changes (e.g., mother gets one-third if no child and no siblings).
3
Study the Quranic proof
The passage cites the verse 'And for his parents, for each of them one sixth of what he leaves if he has a child' (4:11). This is the direct evidence for the parent's one-sixth.
The verse explicitly assigns one-sixth when a child exists.
4
Examine the narrational evidence
The author also quotes a narration from Zaid ibn Thabit that specifies the mother's one-sixth when there are two or more siblings.
This supplements the Quranic ruling for the mother.
5
Recognize scholarly difference on grandfather's share
The passage notes that the grandfather receives one-sixth with a child or grandchild. Some schools differ on the grandfather's share when siblings are present.
This is a point of ikhtilaf among madhahib.

[۱۳۲۱۰ (۱۲) چھٹا حصہ سات لوگوں کا حصہ ہے (۱) ماں باپ میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے بیٹے یا پوتے کے ساتھ (۲) اور ماں کے لئے بھائیوں کے ساتھ (۳) اور چھٹا ہے دادی کے لئے (۴) اور دادا کے لئے اولاد کے ساتھ اور پوتے کے ساتھ (۵) اور پوتیوں کے لئے ایک بیٹی کے ساتھ (۶) اور علاتی بہنوں کے لئے ایک حقیقی بہن کے ساتھ ( ۷ ) اور ایک اخیافی بہن کے لئے،

وجه
(۳) ماں نہ ہو تو دادی کو چھٹا ملے گا۔
And the one-sixth is the prescribed share for seven: each of the parents with the child or grandchild; and the mother with brothers; and the one-sixth is for the grandmother; and the grandfather with child and grandchild; and granddaughters with one daughter; and consanguine sisters with one full sister; and one uterine sibling. Explanation of each category with Quranic proofs and narrations.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven categories of heirs who receive the one-sixth share (suds) in Hanafi inheritance law. They are: (1) each parent when there is a child or grandchild; (2) the mother when there are siblings; (3) the grandmother when the mother is absent; (4) the grandfather with a child or grandchild; (5) granddaughters when there is one daughter; (6) consanguine sisters when there is one full sister; (7) a single uterine sibling. The author cites Quranic verses (e.g., An-Nisa 4:11-12) and narrations from Zaid ibn Thabit to substantiate each category. The commentary emphasizes that the one-sixth is a fixed share that is not affected by the residue, and it is given under specific conditions mentioned in the text.

Key Terms
السدس (al-suds): The one-sixth fixed share.
الفرض (al-fard): A prescribed share in inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is one of the seven categories that receive one-sixth?
A) A full sister when there is a father
B) A consanguine sister when there is one full sister
C) A private tutor
D) A grandfather when there is no child

Key Takeaway
The one-sixth is a fixed share for seven categories, each conditional on specific heirs; correct identification of these categories is essential for valid inheritance distribution.

The Seven Heirs Entitled to One-Sixth (السدس)
Listing the seven one-sixth heirs with proofs and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of heirs who receive one-sixth (السدس) in Hanafi faraid and identify the condition that triggers each share.

Core Idea
Seven heirs receive one-sixth: parents with child, mother with siblings, grandmother without mother, grandfather with child, granddaughters with one daughter, consanguine sisters with full sister, single uterine sibling.

The one-sixth share (السدس) is one of the six fixed Quranic shares in inheritance. This lesson, based on Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, enumerates the seven categories of heirs entitled to this share under specific conditions. We will explore each category, its conditions, and the textual evidence from Quran and Sunnah, including an example calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven categories from the text
Read the list: (1) mother/father with child, (2) mother with siblings, (3) grandmother without mother, (4) grandfather with child/grandson, (5) granddaughters with one daughter, (6) consanguine sisters with full sister, (7) single uterine sibling.
The text groups these under 'السدس فرض سبعة'.
2
For each category, state the condition
For parents: existence of child/grandson. For mother: existence of 2+ siblings. For grandmother: absence of mother. For grandfather: existence of child/grandson. For granddaughters: one daughter present. For consanguine sisters: one full sister present. For uterine sibling: single sibling only.
Conditions prevent over/under inheritance.
3
Identify the proof for each category
The text provides Quranic verse for parents and mother with siblings (4:11). For grandmother and grandfather, it gives hadiths. For others, it references sahabi practice.
The proofs are dalil naqli.
4
Understand the practical application
Note that grandfather can also take residue as asabah, but grandmother cannot. Work through the example: grandmother gets 1/6, son gets 5/6.
The example shows a simple case.
5
Compare with other schools
The Hanafi school includes grandfather with child; Shafi'i gives grandfather only if no child. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Cross-madhhab awareness.

ان السدس الآخر طعمة (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی میراث الجد ، ص ۴۵ نمبر ۲۸۹۶ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی میراث الجد ، ص ۳۰ نمبر ۲۰۹۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دادا کے ساتھ بیٹا یا پوتا ہوتو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ اور اگر کوئی نہ ہو تو اس چھٹے کے علاوہ عصبہ کے طور پر مزیدل جائے گا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے دادی کے لئے چھٹا حصہ متعین کیا جب کہ اس سے نیچے ہاں نہ ہو (ب) پھر دوسری دادی حضرت عمرؓ کے پاس آئی اور اپنی میراث مانگنے لگی تو فرمایا کتاب اللہ میں تمہارا کچھ نہیں ہے۔ جو فیصلہ تمہارے علاوہ کے لئے ہوا اس سے زیادہ کرنے والا نہیں ہوں۔ اور وہ چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ اگر تم دونوں اس میں شریک ہو جاؤ تو تم دونوں کے درمیان (12) And one-sixth is the share of seven: for each of the two parents with the child or child's son, and it is the sixth. From this narration it is known that if there are more than one uterine sibling, they receive one-third. And the siblings will be given equally. Lafz walad al-um: uterine sibling. (12) One-sixth is the share of seven people: (1) For each of the mother and father with a son or grandson, (2) and for the mother with brothers, (3) and one-sixth is for the grandmother, (4) and for the grandfather with children and with a grandson, (5) and for granddaughters with one daughter, (6) and for consanguine sisters with one full sister, (7) and for one uterine brother/sister. These seven types of people receive one-sixth. The detail of each is: (1) If with the mother there is a son of the deceased or a grandson, similarly with the father there is a son of the deceased, then the mother and father get one-sixth. And if there is no daughter or grandson, it has passed before that the mother has one-third. The proof of this is in the verse: 'And for his parents, for each of them one-sixth of what he leaves if he has a child; but if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then his mother has one-third; and if he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth after a will' (Surah an-Nisa 4). This verse states that if there is a son (and if not, a grandson is in the position of a son), then the parents have one-sixth. (2) The narration has passed from Zaid ibn Thabit: 'And the interpretation is the interpretation of Abu al-Zinad according to the meanings of Zaid. He said: The inheritance of the mother from her child when her son or daughter dies, leaving a child or a grandchild, male or female, or leaving two siblings or more, male or female, from both parents or from the father or from the mother, is one-sixth.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Fard al-Umm, vol. 6, p. 1372, no. 12294) In this narration, if there is a son or a grandson or two siblings, the mother and parents get one-sixth. (2) The second case is that if there are many brothers, the mother gets one-sixth. (1) The verse has passed: 'if he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth' (Surah an-Nisa 4). (2) And the narration also passed: 'or leaving two siblings or more, male or female, from both parents or from the father or from the mother, [then] one-sixth' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Fard al-Umm, vol. 6, p. 372, no. 12294). In this narration also, if there are many brothers or sisters, the mother gets one-sixth. (3) If there is no mother, then the grandmother gets one-sixth. (4) If there is no father, then the grandfather gets one-sixth with a son or grandson. And if there is none, then besides one-sixth, he gets an additional one-sixth as an asabah. A hadith: 'From Abu Buraidah from his father that the Prophet ﷺ assigned one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother below her' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Sajdah, p. 45, no. 2895; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi Mirath al-Jaddah, p. 130, no. 2100). From this hadith it is known that if there is no mother, the grandmother gets one-sixth. If there are multiple grandmothers, they all share that one-sixth. Then another grandmother came to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking about her inheritance. He said: 'There is nothing in the Book of Allah for you. And the judgment that was given was only for someone else. I am not one to add to the shares. But it is that one-sixth. If you both come together in it, it is between you. And whichever of you is alone, it is hers.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Jaddah, p. 25, no. 2894; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi Mirath al-Jaddah, p. 30, no. 2101). From this narration it is known that if there are multiple grandmothers, they all get that one-sixth, and they divide it. The problem will be constructed like this: Deceased 100, grandmother 16.66, son 83.34. In this, the grandmother is given one-sixth and the rest to the son. And if there is no son or grandson, she still gets one-sixth. She does not get anything extra as an asabah because the grandmother is not an asabah. (4) If there is no father, the grandfather gets one-sixth with a son or grandson. And if there is none, besides receiving one-sixth, he gets an additional one-sixth as an asabah. A hadith: 'From Imran ibn Husain that a man came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: My grandson died. What do I have from his inheritance? He said: You have one-sixth. When he turned away, he called him and said: You have another sixth. When he turned away, he called him and said: That other sixth is a gift (asabah).' (Abu Dawud, Bab ma ja'a fi Mirath al-Jaddah, p. 45, no. 2896; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi Mirath al-Jaddah, p. 30, no. 2099). In this hadith, if the grandfather has a son or grandson, he gets one-sixth; and if there is none, besides that one-sixth, he gets more as an asabah.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of inheritance (faraid). It expands on the seventh category of fard (Quranic share) — the one-sixth (السدس). The author lists seven types of heirs who are entitled to one-sixth under specific conditions. The first category is the mother and father when the deceased leaves a child or a son's child (grandson). The proof is Quran 4:11, which explicitly gives each parent one-sixth when there is a child. The second category is the mother when there are siblings (two or more). The same verse says 'if he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth.' The third category is the grandmother (paternal) when the mother is absent. The passage cites a hadith from Abu Buraidah that the Prophet (ﷺ) gave one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother. The fourth is the grandfather (paternal) when the deceased leaves a child or grandson. The hadith from Imran ibn Husain shows the grandfather gets one-sixth, and if no child, he gets the sixth plus the residue as an asabah (male agnate). The fifth category is granddaughters (sons' daughters) when there is one daughter — they share the one-sixth with the daughter. The sixth is consanguine sisters (paternal half-sisters) when there is one full sister — they get one-sixth. The seventh is a single uterine brother or sister (maternal half-sibling) — they get one-sixth if alone. The passage also explains the case of multiple grandmothers: they share the one-sixth equally, as per the incident of Umar ibn al-Khattab with two grandmothers. An example calculation is provided: deceased leaves 100, grandmother gets 16.66 (one-sixth), and the remaining 83.34 goes to the son. The grandmother never takes as asabah because she is not an agnate. For the grandfather, if there is no child, he takes one-sixth in addition to the residue as an asabah, because he is an agnate. The entire discussion is within the Hanafi school, relying on Quran, hadith, and sahabi practice.

Key Terms
السدس (as-sudus): One-sixth, a Quranic fixed share (fard) given to seven categories of heirs under specified circumstances.
فرض (fard): A fixed share prescribed by the Quran or Sunnah for a specific heir.
عصبة (asabah): An agnate heir who takes the residue after the Quranic shares are distributed; typically male relatives through the father's line.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is one of the seven categories of heirs who receive one-sixth (السدس) according to the Hanafi school?
A) The mother when the deceased has no siblings
B) The grandmother when the deceased has no mother
C) The daughter when there is a son
D) The paternal uncle when there is no father

Key Takeaway
The one-sixth share (السدس) is a fixed Quranic share assigned to seven categories of heirs under specific conditions, reflecting the balance between close and distant relatives in Hanafi inheritance law.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
6 min
Grandmother's Share of 1/6 in Hanafi Faraid
Ruling on grandmothers inheriting 1/6 with proof from hadith and companion athar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the grandmother's share (1/6) under Hanafi faraid, identify the condition (absence of mother), and apply the rule when multiple grandmothers are present.

Core Idea
Grandmothers inherit a single 1/6 share, shared among them, when the mother is absent.

This lesson examines the fixed share of the grandmother in Hanafi inheritance law. We will see the primary proof from the Prophet's hadith and the guidance of Umar ibn al-Khattab. The ruling is clear: the grandmother receives one-sixth, but only when there is no mother. If multiple grandmothers exist, they divide this single sixth among themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The inheritance share of the grandmother (jaddah). The ruling: she receives one-sixth (suds) as a fixed share (fard).
The share is fard because it is a prescribed portion.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is a hadith from Abu Buraydah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother beneath her. A secondary proof is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab for multiple grandmothers.
The hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut, but accepted in faraid.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'jalla lil-jaddati al-suds' directly allocates a specific share. The condition 'idha lam takun dunaha umm' limits the share to cases where no mother exists. This yields the rule: grandmother takes 1/6 only when mother is absent.
The word 'jalla' indicates an assignment, not a mere recommendation.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Example: deceased leaves grandmother and son. Grandmother gets 1/6 (e.g., 16.66 out of 100), son gets the remainder (83.34) as asabah. If multiple grandmothers, they share the 1/6 equally.
The grandmother does not get any residue as asabah; she is not an asabah heir.

حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي بريدة عن ابيه ان النبى الله جعل للجدة السدس اذا لم تكن دونها ام (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في السجدة ص ۴۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۵ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی میراث الجدة ، ص ۱۳۰، نمبر ۲۱۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماں نہ ہو تو دادی کو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔
کئی دادیاں ہو تو سب کو چھٹے حصے ہی میں شریک ہونا ہوگا۔
ثم جاءت الجدة الاخرى الى عمر بن الخطاب تسأله ميراثها فقال مالک فی کتاب الله شيء وماكان القضاء الذي قضى به الا لغيرك وما انا بزائد فى الفرائض ولكن هو ذلك السدس فان اجتمعتما فيه فهو بينكما وايتكما ما خلت به فهو لها (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی الجدة ، ص ۲۵، نمبر ۲۸۹۴ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی میراث الجدة ، ص ۳۰ نمبر ۲۱۰۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی دادیاں ہوں تو سب کو چھٹا حصہ ہی ملے گا۔ اس میں تقسیم کرے۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔
میت 100
دادی
بیٹا
16.66
83.34
اس میں دادی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا اور باقی بیٹے کو دیا۔ اور اگر بیٹا اور پوتا نہ ہوتب بھی چھٹا ہی ملے گا۔ عورت ہونے کی وجہ سے مزید عصبہ کے طور پر کچھ نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ دادی عصبہ نہیں ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے دادی کے لئے چھٹا حصہ متعین کیا جب کہ اس سے نیچے ماں نہ ہو (ب) پھر دوسری دادی حضرت عمرؓ کے پاس آئی اور اپنی میراث مانگنے لگی تو فرمایا کتاب اللہ میں تمہارا کچھ نہیں ہے۔ جو فیصلہ تمہارے علاوہ کے لئے ہوا اس سے زیادہ کرنے والا نہیں ہوں۔ اور وہ چھٹا حصہ ہے۔ اگر تم دونوں اس میں شریک ہو جاؤ تو تم دونوں کے درمیان ہوگا اور جو لے اڑی وہ لے اڑی
In a hadith: From Abu Buraydah from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother beneath her. (Sunan Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Fara'id, no. 2895; Tirmidhi, no. 2100). From this hadith it is understood that when there is no mother, the grandmother gets one-sixth. If there are multiple grandmothers, they all share in that one-sixth. Then another grandmother came to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking about her inheritance. He said: 'There is nothing for you in the Book of Allah, and the judgment that was given was only for someone else, and I am not one to increase in the prescribed shares. But it is that one-sixth. If both of you come together in it, it is between you, and whichever of you is alone with it, it is hers.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Fara'id, no. 2894; Tirmidhi, no. 2101). From this effect it is understood that when there are multiple grandmothers, they all get one-sixth; they distribute it among themselves. The scenario is such: Deceased: 100. Grandmother: 16.66, Son: 83.34. In this, the grandmother is given one-sixth, and the remainder to the son. And if there is no son or grandson, she still gets one-sixth. She does not get any additional share as asabah because she is a female, for the grandmother is not an asabah. Marginal note: (a) The Prophet assigned one-sixth for the grandmother when there is no mother beneath her. (b) Then a second grandmother came to Umar and asked for her inheritance; he said: 'There is nothing for you in the Book of Allah, and the judgment that was given was only for someone else, and I am not one to increase in the prescribed shares. But it is that one-sixth. If both of you come together in it, it is between you, and whichever of you is alone with it, it is hers.'
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the grandmother's inheritance share, supported by two proofs. The first proof is a hadith from Abu Buraydah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigns one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother. The second proof is an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab, who judged that multiple grandmothers share the one-sixth. The commentator then provides a calculation example: a deceased leaves 100 units, a grandmother and a son. The grandmother takes one-sixth (16.66), and the son takes the remainder (83.34). The ruling is that the grandmother gets only one-sixth, no more, and she cannot take the residue as asabah because she is not an asabah heir. The marginal notes explain the two proofs in further detail.

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother (paternal or maternal) who inherits when the mother is absent.
سدس (suds): One-sixth share, a fixed Quranic share.
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heirs who take the remainder after fixed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What share does a grandmother receive when the mother is not present?
A) 1/8
B) 1/6
C) 1/3
D) 1/4

Key Takeaway
The grandmother inherits one-sixth only when no mother exists; multiple grandmothers share that single sixth.

Grandfather's Share: 1/6 Plus Residue
Ruling on grandfather inheriting 1/6 with son/grandson, else 1/6 plus residue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the grandfather's inheritance share in the Hanafi school and determine whether he receives only the fixed 1/6 or also the residue.

Core Idea
The grandfather inherits 1/6 as a fixed share, and when no son/grandson exists, he also takes the residue as asabah.

In Hanafi faraid, the paternal grandfather takes the place of the father when the father is absent. His share depends on the presence of a son or grandson. This lesson explains the dual nature of his inheritance: a fixed portion and an optional residuary share, backed by a clear hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the absence of the father
The grandfather only inherits if the father is deceased. Confirm that the grandfather is the paternal grandfather and the father is not alive.
If the father is alive, the grandfather is excluded.
2
Check for a son or grandson
Determine whether the deceased left a son or a son's son (however low). If such a descendant exists, the grandfather gets only one-sixth.
The presence of a son or grandson blocks the residue.
3
Calculate the share when a son/grandson exists
The grandfather receives 1/6 of the estate as a prescribed fixed share (fard). The residue goes to the son/grandson as asabah.
No additional share for the grandfather.
4
Calculate the share when no son/grandson exists
The grandfather first takes 1/6 as fard, then inherits the remaining estate as asabah. This is often expressed as '1/6 plus residue'.
He effectively gets two sixths: one prescribed, one through residue.
5
Apply the hadith as proof
The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn shows the Prophet giving first one-sixth, then another sixth as a gift, indicating the grandfather's residuary right. This supports the Hanafi position.
The additional sixth is called 'tumah' (gift), meaning residue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) باپ نہ ہو تو دادا کے لئے بیٹے یا پوتے کے ساتھ چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ اور کوئی نہ ہو تو چھٹا حصہ ملنے کے علاوہ عصبہ کے طور پر مزید چھٹا حصہ مل جاتا ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عمران بن حصین ان رجلا اتى النبى الله الله فقال ان ابن ابنی مات فمالی من ميراثه ؟ قال لك السدس ، فلما ادبر دعاه فقال لك سدس آخر فلما ادبر دعاه فقال ان السدس الآخر طعمة (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی میراث الجد ، ص ۴۵ نمبر ۲۸۹۶ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی میراث الجد ، ص ۳۰ نمبر ۲۰۹۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دادا کے ساتھ بیٹا یا پوتا ہوتو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ اور اگر کوئی نہ ہو تو اس چھٹے کے علاوہ عصبہ کے طور پر مزید مل جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (ج) ایک آدمی حضور کے پاس آیا اور کہا میرا پوتا انتقال کر گیا ہے مجھے اس کے ترکے سے کیا ملے گا۔ فرمایا تجھ کو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ پھر جب واپس لوٹا تو حضور نے فرمایا تمہارے لئے دوسرا چھٹا بھی ہے۔ پھر جب واپس لوٹا تو اس کو بلایا اور فرمایا یہ دوسرا چھٹا عصبہ کے طور پر ہے۔
(4) When the father is not present, the grandfather gets one-sixth along with a son or grandson. And if there is no one else (i.e., no son or grandson), then besides the one-sixth, he gets an additional residue as asabah. In a hadith: From Imran ibn Husayn that a man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'My grandson died; what do I get from his inheritance?' He said: 'You have one-sixth.' When he turned away, He called him and said: 'You have another sixth.' When he turned away, He called him and said: 'That other sixth is a gift.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Fara'id, no. 2896; Tirmidhi, no. 2099). This hadith shows that when the grandfather has a son or grandson with him, he gets one-sixth; and if there is no one else, he gets the first sixth and then an additional sixth as asabah. Marginal note: (c) A man came to the Prophet and said: 'My grandson has passed away; what do I get from his estate?' He said: 'You get one-sixth.' When he turned back, the Prophet said: 'You have another sixth.' When he turned back again, he called him and said: 'That second sixth is as asabah.'
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the grandfather's inheritance when the father is absent. If grandfather is with a son or grandson, he gets one-sixth. If there are no such descendants, he gets one-sixth plus an additional one-sixth as a residuary heir (asabah). The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn is cited as proof: a man asked about his grandson's inheritance, and the Prophet first said one-sixth, then called him back to give another sixth which is a gift (meaning residue). The marginal note clarifies that the second sixth is asabah. Thus, the grandfather can take residue, unlike the grandmother.

Key Terms
جد (jadd): Paternal grandfather who inherits in place of the father.
طعمة (tumah): A gift or additional grant; in this hadith it refers to the residue as asabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does a grandfather receive when there is no son or grandson?
A) Only 1/6
B) 1/6 plus residue
C) Only residue
D) 1/3

Key Takeaway
The grandfather's inheritance is 1/6 when a son/grandson exists, and 1/6 plus residue when there is none, based on the hadith of the 'two sixths'.

Granddaughters' Share of 1/6 with One Daughter
Ruling with hadith proof and numerical example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of agnatic granddaughters when one daughter survives and no son, using the Hanafi rule of completing the two-thirds share.

Core Idea
When one daughter gets half, granddaughters receive one-sixth to complete the two-thirds due to daughters.

This lesson addresses a specific Hanafi inheritance rule: when a deceased leaves one daughter and no son, agnatic granddaughters (daughters of a predeceased son) are not excluded. Instead, they receive one-sixth to bring the total share of female descendants to two-thirds, based on a direct Prophetic ruling. You will learn the proof from hadith and apply it in a calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the surviving heirs
List the heirs: one daughter, one or more agnatic granddaughters (through a predeceased son), and possibly other heirs like a sister. Note that there is no son.
Granddaughters are agnatic (bint al-ibn) and inherit in place of their deceased father.
2
Determine the daughter's share
The single daughter receives a fixed half (1/2) as a Quranic heir.
If there were two or more daughters, they would share two-thirds.
3
Apply the principle of takmilah al-thuluthayn
To bring the female descendants' total to two-thirds, the granddaughters collectively receive one-sixth (1/6). The daughter's half (1/2) plus granddaughters' 1/6 equals 2/3.
This principle is specific to Hanafi law, derived from the hadith.
4
Cite the hadith proof
Recall the hadith where the Prophet gave a granddaughter 1/6 to complete 2/3 when a daughter inherited half, and the remainder to the sister.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Musa and recorded in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
5
Calculate shares numerically
Assume an estate of 100. Daughter: 50 (1/2), granddaughter(s): 16.66 (1/6), sister (if any): 33.33 (residue). Adjust if more than one granddaughter: they share the 1/6 equally.
The example in the text uses a sister as the residuary heir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) پوتیوں کے لئے ایک بیٹی کے ساتھ یعنی ایک بیٹی ہو اور بیٹا نہ ہو تو دو ثلث پورا کرنے کے لئے پوتیوں کو چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک بیٹی کو آدھا ملے گا۔ اور پوتیوں کا چھٹا حصہ ملا تو دونوں ملا کر دو تہائی ہو جائے گی۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ سئل ابوموسى عن ابنه وابنة ابن واخت ... اقضى فيها بما قضى النبي الله للابنة النصف ولابنة الابن السدس تكملة الثلثين وما بقى فللاخت (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب میراث ابنة ابن مع ابنة ص ۱۹۹۷، نمبر ۶۷۳۶ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی میراث الصلب ص ۱۴۴، نمبر ۲۸۹۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک بیٹی ہو تو اس کو آدھا ملے گا۔ اور دو ثلث پورا کرنے کے لئے پوتی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا۔ کیونکہ دو بیٹیوں کو ثلث ملتا ہے ۔ مسئلہ اس طرح ہے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابوموسی سے پوچھا بیٹی، پوتی اور بہن ہو تو کتنا ملے گا؟ فرمایا اس میں وہی فیصلہ کروں گا جو حضور نے کیا۔ بیٹی کے لئے آدھا اور پوتی کے لئے چھٹا دو تہائی پوری کرنے کے لئے اور ایک تہائی بہن کے لئے۔
(5) For granddaughters along with one daughter: when there is one daughter and no son, to complete two-thirds, the granddaughters get one-sixth. Because the daughter gets half, and adding the granddaughters' one-sixth makes two-thirds. In a hadith: Abu Musa was asked about (the shares of) a daughter, a granddaughter, and a sister... He said: 'I will judge in this as the Prophet judged: for the daughter half, for the granddaughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds; and what remains is for the sister.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Kitab al-Fara'id, no. 6736; Abu Dawud, no. 2890). This hadith shows that when there is one daughter, she gets half; and to complete two-thirds, the granddaughter is given one-sixth, because two daughters get two-thirds. The scenario is: Deceased: 100. One daughter, one granddaughter, sister. Daughter: 50 (half), granddaughter: 16.66 (one-sixth), sister: 33.33 (residue one-third). Marginal note: (a) Abu Musa was asked: 'If there is a daughter, a granddaughter, and a sister, how much does each get?' He said: 'I will judge as the Prophet judged: daughter half, granddaughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and one-third for the sister.'
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage addresses the share of granddaughters (daughters of son) when there is one daughter and no son. The ruling is that granddaughters receive one-sixth to complete the two-thirds share that would go to two daughters. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a granddaughter one-sixth with a daughter. A calculation example is provided: deceased leaves 100, one daughter gets 50 (half), one granddaughter gets 16.66 (one-sixth), and a sister gets the remaining 33.33 (one-third). The marginal note summarizes the hadith of Abu Musa.

Key Terms
بنت الابن (bint al-ibn): Granddaughter through a son (agnatic granddaughter).
تكملة الثلثين (takmilah al-thuluthayn): Completing the two-thirds share; when a single daughter gets half, granddaughters get one-sixth to reach two-thirds.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, agnatic granddaughters inherit one-sixth when there is one daughter, completing the two-thirds share for female descendants.

Half-Sister from Father's Share of 1/6
Ruling with proof on half-sister from father's share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the share of a half-sister from the father when a full sister is present, applying the Hanafi rule of completing the two-thirds share.

Core Idea
When a full sister takes half, the half-sister from father gets one-sixth to complete two-thirds.

In Hanafi faraid, the combination of a full sister and a half-sister from the father triggers a specific distribution. The full sister receives half, and to reach the two-thirds that two full sisters would receive, the half-sister is given one-sixth. The remainder goes to any half-brother from the father. Let's explore the proof and a worked example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List all surviving heirs: one full sister (shaqiqah), one half-sister from father (consanguine), and one half-brother from father (consanguine).
The half-sister from father is also called 'alati' sister.
2
Assign Quranic shares
The full sister gets 1/2 (fard) as a single full sister. The half-sister from father gets 1/6 (fard) to complete the 2/3 share that two full sisters would get. The half-brother from father gets the residue as asabah.
This is the Hanafi ruling; some schools disagree.
3
Check the proof
The ruling is based on the athar of Abdullah ibn Zaid (Sahabi) recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi. The statement explicitly assigns 1/6 to sisters from father to complete two-thirds.
The athar is a qawl sahabi, which is a source in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Calculate using the base number
The base number (asl al-mas'alah) is the LCM of the denominators: 2 and 6 → 6. Full sister gets 3/6, half-sister gets 1/6, half-brother gets the remaining 2/6.
Fractions are 3/6 + 1/6 + 2/6 = 1.
5
Apply to an estate
Using the example from the text: estate = 100. Full sister: 50 (half), half-sister: 16.666 (1/6), half-brother: 33.333 (residue).
Check that the sum equals the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۶) باپ شریک بہن کو ماں باپ شریک بہن کے ساتھ چھٹا ملے گا۔ اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ حقیقی بہن موجود ہو تو باپ شریک کا درجہ بعد میں ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک بہن حقیقی ہے یعنی ماں باپ شریک ہے اس لئے اس کو آدھا مل جائے گا اور دو تہائی پورا کرنے کے لئے باپ شریک بہن جس کو علاتی بہن کہتے ہیں اس کو چھٹا حصہ مل جائے گا۔
اثر میں ہے۔ وفى قول عبد الله بن زيد للاخت من الاب والام النصف وللاخوات من الاب السدس تكملة الثلثين وما بقى للاخ من الاب (ب) (سنن البیهقی ، باب میراث الاخوة والاخوات لاب وام اولاب، ج سادس ص ۳۸۱، نمبر ۱۳۳۲۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باپ شریک بہن کو ایک حقیقی بہن کے ساتھ چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔

حاشیہ : (ب) عبد الله بن زید نے فرمایا ایک حقیقی بہن کے لئے آدھا اور باپ شریک بہن کے لئے چھٹا دو تہائی پوری کرنے کے لئے اور باقی باپ شریک بھائی کے لئے۔
(6) A half-sister from the father along with a full sister (from both parents) gets one-sixth. The detail: When a full sister exists, the half-sister's rank comes after. Therefore, the full sister (from both parents) gets half, and to complete two-thirds, the half-sister from the father (called 'alati sister') gets one-sixth. In an athar: In the saying of Abdullah ibn Zaid: 'For the sister from father and mother, half; for the sisters from father, one-sixth to complete two-thirds; and the remainder is for the brother from father.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Kitab al-Fara'id, no. 13327). From this athar it is understood that a half-sister from father gets one-sixth with one full sister. The scenario is: Deceased: 100. One full sister, one half-sister from father, one half-brother from father. Full sister: 50 (half), half-sister: 16.66 (one-sixth), half-brother: 33.33 (residue). Marginal note: (b) Abdullah ibn Zaid said: 'For a full sister, half; for a half-sister from father, one-sixth to complete two-thirds; and the remainder for the half-brother from father.'
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage explains the share of a half-sister from the father's side (consanguine sister) when a full sister is present. The full sister takes half, and to make the two-thirds share that two full sisters would take, the half-sister gets one-sixth. The proof is an athar from Abdullah ibn Zaid, quoted in Sunan al-Bayhaqi. A calculation example is given: deceased leaves 100, one full sister gets 50 (half), one half-sister gets 16.66 (one-sixth), and one half-brother gets the remaining 33.33 as residue. The marginal note restates the athar.

Key Terms
أخت من الأب (ukht min al-ab): Half-sister from father's side (consanguine sister), same father but different mother.
أخت شقيقة (ukht shaqiqah): Full sister from both parents (germane sister).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing
B) 1/2
C) 1/6
D) 1/3

Key Takeaway
The half-sister from the father inherits one-sixth when a single full sister exists, completing the two-thirds share for sisters.

Share of the Uterine Sister (1/6)
Ruling on uterine sister's 1/6

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the share of a uterine sister when there is no descendant and identify the condition that triggers this share.

Core Idea
A single uterine sibling inherits 1/6 when no descendant exists.

This lesson introduces the faraid ruling for a half-sister from the mother's side (uterine sister). She is entitled to one-sixth of the estate, but only if the deceased left no child or grandchild. Understanding this share is essential for accurate inheritance distribution. The passage also implies the same share for a uterine brother, and we will extend to the case of multiple uterine siblings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir
The passage states 'half-sister from mother (ukht li-umm)'. Recognize her as a uterine sibling, distinct from consanguine or germane siblings.
Also called 'akhafi sister' in Urdu.
2
Check the condition
The share of 1/6 applies only when there is no descendant (son, daughter, or grandson). If a descendant exists, uterine siblings are excluded.
Descendants block all uterine siblings completely.
3
Assign the share
If the condition is met, a single uterine sister gets 1/6 of the estate. The same applies to a single uterine brother.
Multiple uterine siblings share 1/3 equally, regardless of gender.
4
Extend to multiple uterine siblings
Although the passage only mentions a single sister, the established rule is: if there are two or more uterine siblings (brothers and/or sisters), they collectively receive 1/3, divided equally among them.
This is based on Quran 4:12.

Grandmother Excluded by Mother
Ruling on hajb of grandmother by mother with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the mother excludes all grandmothers from inheritance and identify the hadith proof supporting this.

Core Idea
The mother's presence removes the grandmother's share entirely.

This lesson explains a key principle of hajb in Hanafi faraid: the grandmother is excluded when the mother is alive. We will look at the hadith that directly supports this ruling and understand the concept of priority in shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Understand that if the mother is present, the grandmother receives no share of inheritance regardless of whether she is paternal or maternal.
The term 'dadi' in the text refers to paternal grandmother, but the hadith uses 'jaddah' which covers both.
2
Understand the principle of priority
Recognize that closer relatives (like mother) exclude more distant ones (like grandmother) in the order of inheritance.
This is a general rule in faraid: the nearer heir blocks the farther.
3
Examine the hadith proof
Read the hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud: the Prophet assigned one-sixth to the grandmother 'when there is no mother below her' – this conditions the grandmother's share on the mother's absence.
The phrase 'اذا لم تكن دونها ام' is the key evidence for exclusion.
4
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine whether the mother is present; if yes, the grandmother is excluded; if no, the grandmother gets one-sixth.
This application is straightforward based on the hadith condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۲۱۱ (۱۳) دادی ، ماں کی وجہ سے ساقط ہوگی۔ ماں موجود ہو تو دادی کو حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ وہ نہیں ہوگی تو دادی کو حصہ ملے گا۔ حصوں میں مقدم اور مؤخر کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے جو پہلے ہوتا ہے اس کو حصہ ملتا ہے۔ وہ نہ ہو تو بعد والے کو ملتا ہے۔ یہاں ماں موجود ہے اس لئے دادی کو نہیں ملے گا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن بريدة عن ابيه ان النبى الله جعل للجدة السدس اذا لم تكن دونها ام (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الجدة ص ۳۵ نمبر ۲۸۹۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دادی کے لئے چھٹا حصہ ہے بشرطیکہ ماں نہ ہو۔ اس لئے ماں سے دادی ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
Grandmother is excluded by the mother. If the mother is present, the grandmother will not receive a share. If she (mother) is not present, the grandmother will receive a share. In shares, precedence and postponement are considered; the one who comes earlier receives a share, and if that one is not present, the later one receives. Here the mother is present, so the grandmother will not receive. (2) There is proof of this in the hadith: from Ibn Buraydah from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother below her. This hadith states that the grandmother gets one-sixth on condition that the mother is not present. Therefore, the grandmother is excluded by the mother.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the exclusion (hajb) of the grandmother by the mother in inheritance. It establishes that if the mother is alive, all grandmothers (paternal and maternal) are excluded from inheritance. The rationale is based on precedence: closer relatives exclude more distant ones. The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) specified one-sixth for the grandmother only when there is no mother. This shows that the mother, being a primary heir, eliminates the grandmother's share. The commentary follows the order: first states the ruling, then explains the principle of priority, then provides the proof, and concludes with the application.

Key Terms
دادی (dadi): Paternal grandmother (mother's mother is also included in 'grandmothers' but the context often refers to paternal grandmother; however, the ruling applies to all grandmothers as per the hadith 'jaddah' which includes both paternal and maternal).
ماں (maan): Mother of the deceased. She is a primary heir and excludes grandmothers.
ساقط (saqit): Excluded from inheritance; the person does not receive any share due to the presence of a closer relative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Father
B) Mother
C) Son
D) Husband

Key Takeaway
The mother excludes all grandmothers from inheritance, confirmed by the Prophetic hadith.

Exclusion of Uterine Siblings in Hanafi Inheritance
Ruling on exclusion of uterine siblings with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of heirs that exclude uterine siblings, explain the Quranic proof for each, and apply the rule to a given inheritance scenario.

Core Idea
Uterine siblings are excluded by child, grandchild, father, and grandfather — four close blood ties take priority.

In Hanafi faraid, uterine siblings (those sharing only the mother) are Quranic heirs but are easily excluded by closer relatives. This passage from al-Sameri lists the four categories that block them: the deceased’s child, grandchild, father, and paternal grandfather. The author provides two Quranic verses and an athar to establish the rule, and uses a fortiori reasoning to emphasize the strength of the exclusion. Understanding this rule prevents common mistakes in estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage explicitly states that uterine siblings (walad al-umm) are excluded (sāqiṭ) by one of four relatives. First, confirm who qualifies as a uterine sibling — they are half-siblings sharing only the mother (akhyaafi brothers and sisters). Then note that the four excluders are: (1) son, (2) son's son (grandson), (3) father, (4) paternal grandfather.
The grandfather stands in the father's place; thus he also excludes uterine siblings.
2
Analyze the first Quranic proof (4:12)
The verse grants uterine siblings one‑sixth each only when the deceased is a kalalah — defined as one who leaves no child and no father. The presence of a child or grandchild therefore removes the condition of kalalah, so the uterine sibling is excluded. Trace how the definition of kalalah (no descendant, no ascendant) directly supports exclusion by both child and father.
The author cites Ibn Abbas's definition of kalalah from Sunan al‑Bayhaqi.
3
Analyze the second Quranic proof (4:176) and the a fortiori argument
Verse 4:176 conditions full siblings' inheritance on the absence of a child. Since full siblings (mother's and father's side) are excluded by a child, uterine siblings — who are even less related — are excluded a fortiori (bi al‑awla). This step shows that the child's presence blocks not only full siblings but also the weaker uterine siblings.
The author explicitly states: 'Since full siblings are excluded by children, uterine siblings are excluded a fortiori.'
4
Identify the rule regarding grandfather
When the father is absent, the paternal grandfather takes his place in excluding uterine siblings. This is based on the principle that the grandfather is the root of the father's line (asl al‑ab). Confirm that the grandfather is included in the definition of 'father' for the purpose of kalalah.
The text says: 'Since the father is not present, the grandfather is in the position of the father.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۱۳ (۱۵) ويسقط ولد الام باحد اربعة بالولد وولد الابن والاب والجد. خت ولد الام : ماں کی اولاد، اس سے مراد ماں شریک بھائی اور ماں شریک بہن ہیں جن کو اخیافی بھائی ، اخیافی بہن کہتے ہیں۔ ری ماں کی اولاد جن کو ماں شریک بھائی بہن، جن کو اخیافی بھائی بہن کہتے ہیں وہ چار قسم کے لوگوں سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں (۱) بیٹوں سے (۲) پوتوں سے (۳) باپ سے اور دادا سے یعنی ان چاروں میں سے کوئی ایک موجود ہو تو ماں شریک بھائی بہن کو حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ بیٹے اور پوتے سے ساقط ہوتا ہے اس کی دلیل خود آیت ہے۔ وان كان رجل يورث كلالة او امرأة وله اخ او اخت فلكل واحد منهما السدس (ج) ( آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کلالہ ہو تو اخیافی بہن بھائی کو چھٹا حصہ دیا جائے گا۔ اور کلالہ اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کی اولاد یا پوتا نہ ہو اور نہ والد ہو۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ اولاد ہو یا ہوتا ہو یا باپ ہو تو اخیافی بہن بھائی ساقط ہو جائیں گے۔ اور باپ نہ ہو تو دادا بھی باپ کے درجے میں ہے۔ اس لئے دادا ہوتے وقت بھی اخیافی بھائی بہن ساقط ہوں گے۔ کلالہ کی تفسیر اوپر گزرچکی ہے۔ انه سمع ابن عباس يقول الكلالة الذى لا يدع ولدا ولا والدا (د) (سن للبیہقی ، باب حجب الاخوة والاخوات من کا نوا بالاب والابن وابن الابن، ج سادس، ص ۱۳۶۹، نمبر ۱۲۲۷۵ (۳) بلکہ اولاد کی وجہ سے ماں باپ شریک بھائی بھی ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ تو اخیافی بھائی بہن بدرجہ اولی ساقط ہوں گے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ یستفتونك قل الله يفتيكم في الكلالة ان امرؤ هلک ليس له ولد وله اخت فلها نصف ماترك وهو يرثها ان لم يكن لها ولد (ه ) ( آیت ۱۷۶ ، سورۃ النساء ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اولاد نہ ہو (اور اسی میں پوتا بھی داخل ہے ) تو بھائی بہن وارث ہوں گے۔ اور اگر یہ ہوں تو وہ ساقط ہو جائیں گے۔
Uterine siblings are excluded by one of four: by a child, by a grandchild, by the father, and by the grandfather. 'Khaat' means mother's children; by this is meant uterine (mother's side) brother and uterine sister, who are called 'akhyaafi' brother and 'akhyaafi' sister. So the mother's children, who are called uterine brother and sister, are excluded by four types of people: (1) by sons, (2) by grandsons, (3) by the father, and by the grandfather. That is, if any one of these four is present, the uterine brother and sister do not get a share. The proof for exclusion by son and grandson is the verse itself: 'And if a man is inherited by kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then each of them gets one-sixth.' (Quran 4:12) This verse says that when it is kalalah, the uterine brother and sister are given one-sixth. And kalalah is one who has no child or grandchild and no parent. This means that if there is a child or grandchild or father, the uterine siblings are excluded. And if the father is not present, the grandfather is in the position of the father, so even when the grandfather is present, the uterine siblings are excluded. The interpretation of kalalah has passed earlier: that he heard Ibn Abbas say: 'Kalalah is one who leaves neither child nor father.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on exclusion of brothers and sisters by father, son, and son's son, vol. 6, p. 1369, no. 12275) (3) Rather, even full siblings (mother's father's side) are excluded by children, so uterine siblings are even more excluded. The verse is: 'They ask you for a ruling. Say: Allah gives you a ruling concerning kalalah: If a man dies having no child, and he has a sister, then for her is half of what he left, and he inherits from her if she has no child.' (Quran 4:176) This verse states that if there is no child (and a grandson is included in this), then siblings inherit; and if there is a child, then they are excluded.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the exclusion (hajb) of uterine siblings (those sharing only the mother) in Hanafi inheritance law. Uterine siblings—called 'akhyaafi'—are excluded by four categories of closer relatives: (1) a son (child of the deceased), (2) a grandson (son's son, even if descending), (3) the father, and (4) the paternal grandfather. The text provides two Quranic proofs: verse 4:12, which grants uterine siblings one-sixth only in the case of kalalah (no child or father), and verse 4:176, which discusses kalalah for full siblings but is analogically extended to uterine siblings. An athar (report) from Ibn Abbas confirms the definition of kalalah. The commentary emphasizes that the grandfather, in the absence of the father, stands in the father's position, so he also excludes uterine siblings. Additionally, it notes that since full siblings (from both parents) are excluded by children, uterine siblings are excluded a fortiori (bi al-awla). The passage follows a clear pattern: ruling stated, conditions enumerated, and then proofs provided.

Key Terms
ولد الام (walad al-umm): Uterine siblings: brothers and sisters who share only the same mother with the deceased. They are distinct from full siblings (sharing both parents) and agnatic siblings (sharing only father).
اخیافی (akhyaafi): Another term for uterine brother; from 'اخ' (brother) and 'اف' (a variant denoting mother's side).
کلالہ (kalalah): A deceased who leaves no descendant (child or grandchild) and no ascendant (father or grandfather). This definition is from Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Mother
B) Full sister
C) Paternal grandfather
D) Uncle

Key Takeaway
Uterine siblings are excluded from inheritance by the presence of a child, grandchild, father, or paternal grandfather.

Exclusion of Granddaughters When Daughters Take Two-Thirds
Ruling with proof from Quran and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for excluding granddaughters when daughters take two-thirds and identify the condition requiring a grandson for asabah.

Core Idea
Granddaughters are excluded by daughters unless a grandson makes them asabah.

This lesson addresses a key rule in Hanafi faraid: when the deceased leaves two or more daughters and also grandchildren through a predeceased son, the daughters take two-thirds of the estate, consuming the available shares. Granddaughters are thereby excluded from inheritance unless a grandson is present to serve as their asabah (residuary heir). We will examine the textual proofs from the Quran and the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit, and work through a practical calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary heirs and their shares
Recognize that daughters (banat) are entitled to two-thirds of the estate when two or more exist, as per Quran 4:11. Granddaughters (banat al-ibn) are secondary heirs.
2
State the general ruling of exclusion
When daughters take their two-thirds, there is no residue left for granddaughters. They are excluded unless an exception applies.
3
Identify the exception: the role of a grandson
If a grandson (ibn al-ibn) is present at the same level or lower than the granddaughters, he becomes the residuary heir for the remaining one-third, and the granddaughters become asabah with him, taking half his share.
4
Examine the proofs: Quran and athar
Quran 4:11 fixes the daughters' two-thirds. The athar from Zaid ibn Thabit explicitly states that granddaughters have no inheritance with daughters unless accompanied by a male at their level or below.
5
Apply to a numerical example
Use a sample estate of 100. Two daughters take 66.66. The remaining 33.33 goes to a grandson and granddaughter in a 2:1 ratio (22.22 and 11.11). If no grandson, granddaughter gets nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۲۱۴ (۱۶) واذا استكملت البنات الثلثين سقطت بنات الابن الا ان يكون بازائهن او (۱۳۲۱۴ (۱۶) اگر بیٹیاں دو تہائی لے لیں تو پوتیاں ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں مگر یہ کہ اس کے برابر میں یا ان سے نیچے ہوتا ہوتو ان کو عصبہ بنا دے گا۔ مسئلے میں گزر چکا ہے کہ دو بیٹی ہو یا اس سے زیادہ ہو تو سب کو دو تہائی ہی ملے گی اس سے زیادہ نہیں ۔ اسی میں تمام بیٹیوں کو شرکت کرنی ہوگی ۔ اب پوتیاں ہوں تو ان کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ کیونکہ دو تہائی بیٹیاں لے چکی ہیں۔ اب کچھ باقی نہیں رہا۔ اس لئے پوتیوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ آیت میں ہے کہ دو سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں تب بھی دو تہائی ہی ملے گی۔ يوصيكم الله في اولادكم للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين فان كن نساء فوق اثنتين فلهن ثلثا ما ترك (الف) (آیت اا، سورۃ النساء ۴) البتہ اگر پوتیوں کے ساتھ پوتا ہو یا اس کے نیچے پر پوتا ہو اور بیٹیوں کے دو تہائی لینے کے بعد جو ایک تہائی پیچ گئی ہو وہ پوتوں کو بطور عصب مل رہی ہو تو پوتیوں کو بھی اس میں سے مل جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں پوتوں کو دو گنا اور پوتی کو ایک گنا ملے گا۔ اور پوتیاں بھی پوتوں کے ساتھ عصبہ بن جائے گی۔
اثر میں ہے۔ عن خارجة بن زيد عن ابيه زيد بن ثابت ... وان لم يكن الولد ذكرا وكانتا اثنتين فاكثر من البنات فانه لا ميراث لبنات الابن معهن الا ان يكون مع بنات الابن ذكر هو من المتوفى بمنزلتهن او هو اطرف منهن فيرد على من بمنزلته ومن فوقه من بنات الابناء فضلا ان فضل فيقسمونه للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين فان لم يفضل شيء فلا شيء لهم (ب) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب میراث اولا والا بن ، ج سادس ص ۱۳۷۷، نمبر ۱۲۳۱۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بیٹیوں کے دو تہائی لینے کے بعد پوتیوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔ البتہ اس کے ساتھ یا اس سے نیچے ہوتا ہو و وہ بطور عصبہ لے گا۔ اور پوتیوں کو بھی الذکر مثل حظ الانثیین دے گا۔

حاشیہ : (الف) تم کو اللہ اولاد کے بارے میں وصیت کرتا ہے مرد کے لئے عورت کا دو گنا ہے، پس اگر دو سے زیادہ عورتیں ہوں تو اس کے لئے ترکہ کی دو تہائی ہوگی (ب) زید بن ثابت نے فرمایا اگر مذکر اولاد نہ ہوں اور دو یا اس سے زیادہ بیٹیاں ہوں تو ان کے ساتھ پوتیوں کو میراث نہیں ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ پوتیوں کے ساتھ اسی درجے کا پوتا ہو یا ان سے نیچے کے پوتے ہوں تو لوٹائی جائے گی۔ جو اس درجے میں ہو یا اس سے اوپر کی پوتیاں ہوں تو مال زیادہ ہوا ہو پھر اس کو مرد کے لئے عورتوں کے دو گنا کے طور پر تقسیم کریں گے ۔ اور اگر کچھ نہ بچے تو ان پوتیوں کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہے۔
Lesson 3214 (16): And when the daughters have taken the two-thirds, the granddaughters are excluded, unless there is with them a male [grandson] at their level or below, he makes them asabah. If the daughters take two-thirds, then granddaughters are excluded, unless there is a grandson at their level or below, then he makes them asabah. It has passed in the issue that if there are two daughters or more, they all get only two-thirds, not more. All daughters share in that. Now if there are granddaughters, they get nothing, because the daughters have taken two-thirds, nothing remains. So granddaughters get nothing. The verse says: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is like the share of two females. But if there are more than two females, they get two-thirds of what he leaves.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:11). However, if there is a grandson with the granddaughters, or a grandson below them, and after the daughters take two-thirds, the remaining one-third goes to the grandsons as asabah, then the granddaughters also get a share from it. In that case, the grandsons get double and the granddaughters get one share each. And the granddaughters become asabah with the grandsons. There is an athar: From Kharija ibn Zaid from his father Zaid ibn Thabit: '...and if there is no male child, and there are two or more daughters, then there is no inheritance for granddaughters with them, unless there is with the granddaughters a male [grandson] at their level or lower, then it is returned to those at that level and above from the granddaughters as a surplus if there is a surplus, and they divide it for the male like the share of two females. If there is no surplus, then nothing for them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). In this athar, after the daughters take two-thirds, granddaughters get nothing. But if there is a grandson at their level or below, he takes as asabah, and gives the granddaughters the male gets double the female. The calculation is as follows: Estate 100, two daughters get 66.66, a [grandson] gets 22.22, a [granddaughter] gets 11.11. Here from 100, two-thirds i.e. 66.66 was given to the two daughters. The remaining one-third i.e. 33.33 was distributed between the granddaughter and grandson as asabah. Therefore, the grandson got double 22.22 and the granddaughter got one share 11.11. If there were no grandson, in that case the granddaughter would get nothing. Footnotes: (a) Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is like the share of two females. But if there are more than two females, they get two-thirds of what he leaves. (b) Zaid ibn Thabit said: if there are no male children, and there are two or more daughters, then with them granddaughters have no inheritance, unless there is with the granddaughters a male at their level or lower, then it is returned to those at that level and above from the granddaughters if there is a surplus, and they divide it for the male double the female. If nothing remains, then nothing for them.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the exclusion of granddaughters (banat al-ibn) when daughters (banat) have already taken their maximum share of two-thirds. The matn states that if daughters take two-thirds, granddaughters are excluded unless there is a grandson (ibn al-ibn) at their level or below who makes them asabah. The Urdu commentary explains that two or more daughters share the two-thirds, consuming the entire estate if it is only two-thirds, leaving nothing for granddaughters. The proof is Quran 4:11 which sets the two-thirds limit for daughters. However, if there is a grandson, he becomes residuary heir (asabah) for the remaining one-third, and granddaughters join him as asabah with him, receiving half of his share. The author provides a practical example: with an estate of 100, two daughters get 66.66, and the remaining 33.33 goes to a grandson and granddaughter in a 2:1 ratio. If there is no grandson, the granddaughter gets nothing. The athar from Zaid ibn Thabit confirms this ruling.

Key Terms
بنات الابن (banat al-ibn): Granddaughters (son's daughters).
عصبہ (asabah): Residuary heir who takes remaining estate after fixed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can granddaughters inherit when two or more daughters are present?
A) Always, because they are of the same lineage
B) Never, because daughters take two-thirds
C) Only if there is a grandson at their level or below who acts as asabah
D) Only if the daughters are also granddaughters

Key Takeaway
Granddaughters are excluded by daughters unless accompanied by a grandson who makes them asabah.

6 min
Exclusion of Consanguine Sisters by Full Sisters
Ruling on when full sisters exclude consanguine sisters unless a brother is present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when consanguine sisters are excluded by full sisters, and apply the exception when a consanguine brother is present to calculate their shares.

Core Idea
Full sisters take two-thirds; consanguine sisters excluded unless a brother makes them asabah.

This lesson clarifies a key inheritance rule: when full sisters exist, consanguine sisters (from the father only) are generally excluded from inheriting. However, if a consanguine brother is present, he takes the residue as an asabah heir, and the consanguine sisters share that residue with him. We will examine the proofs from the Quran and hadith, and work through a numerical example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs
List the categories: full sisters (akhawāt li ab wa umm), consanguine sisters (akhawāt li ab), and consanguine brother (akh li ab).
Full sisters are primary; consanguine siblings are secondary.
2
State the default rule
When two or more full sisters exist, they take the fixed share of two-thirds of the estate. Since no residue remains, consanguine sisters are excluded (sāqitah).
This is based on Quran 4:176.
3
Apply the exception
If a consanguine brother is also present, after giving full sisters their two-thirds, the remaining one-third goes to the consanguine brother as asabah. He then shares it with his consanguine sisters in a 2:1 ratio (male double female).
The brother 'makes them asabah' (yuʿaṣṣibuhunna).
4
Cite the proofs
The Quranic verse (4:176) assigns two-thirds to sisters. The hadith from Bayhaqi explicitly states that consanguine sisters get nothing unless a brother is present, and then the residue is divided 2:1.
The hadith provides the 'illa for the exception.
5
Calculate a sample case
Take a base of 100. Full sisters receive 66.66 (two-thirds). The residue 33.33 goes to the consanguine brother and sister, with the brother taking 22.22 and the sister 11.11 (2:1 ratio).
This demonstrates the practical application.

حاشیہ : (الف) اگر لڑکیاں دو سے زیادہ ہوں تو ان کے لئے ترکہ کی دو تہائی ہے۔ اور اگر بھائی بہن مذکر اور مؤنث ہوں تو مرد کے لئے عورت کا دو گنا ہو گا (ب) پس اگر حقیقی دو بہنیں یا زیادہ ہوں تو ان کے لئے دو تہائی ہوگی۔ اور ان کے ہوتے ہوئے باپ شریک بہنوں کی میراث نہیں ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ بہنوں کے ساتھ باپ شریک بھائی ہو۔ پس اگر باپ شریک بھائی ہو تو تقسیم شروع کی جائے گی جس کے لئے حصے ہوں۔ پس ان کو دو، پس اگر اس سے بچ جائے تو باپ شریک بھائی بہن میں تقسیم ہوگی۔ اس اصول پر کہ مرد کے لئے عورت کا دو گنا۔ پس اگر کچھ نہ بچے تو ان کے لئے کچھ نہیں ہوگی۔
Below them is a son's son, so he makes them asabah. And when the full sisters take the two-thirds, the consanguine sisters are excluded unless there is with them a brother of theirs who makes them asabah. (17) If the full sisters receive two-thirds, then the consanguine sisters are excluded unless there is a brother with them who makes them asabah. The case has passed that if there are two full sisters, they get two-thirds, not more. Now if there are two or more sisters, they are given two-thirds. Therefore the consanguine sisters, called 'father's side sisters', get nothing because nothing remains. The verse says: 'If there are two (sisters), they have two-thirds of what he left, and if they are brothers and sisters (mixed), then for the male is the share of two females' (Surah Nisa 4:176). This verse states that two or more sisters get two-thirds. So now consanguine sisters get nothing. However, if there is a brother with those sisters, after the full sisters take their shares, the one-third that remains goes to the brother as asabah. Then among them, the consanguine (father's side) sisters are given in the proportion of male to female: the brother gets double and the sister gets single. This is proven by the athar: 'If the children of the mother and father are two or more females, they are prescribed two-thirds, and there is no inheritance for the daughters of the father except if there is with them a male from the father. If there is a male from the father, begin with the prescribed shares of those who have a prescribed share and give them. Then if there remains a surplus, it is divided among the children of the father, the male having the share of two females. If nothing remains, nothing for them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Inheritance of Full and Consanguine Brothers/Sisters, vol. 6, p. 1381, no. 12326). This athar shows that the full sisters take two-thirds, then what remains goes to the brother as asabah, and from that the consanguine sisters take. The calculation is as follows: Base 100; two full sisters: 66.66; consanguine sister and brother: 11.11 and 22.22. In this case, the base is made 100. Two-thirds i.e., 66.66 is given to full sisters. The remaining one-third i.e., 33.33 is given to the consanguine brother and sister as asabah, where the brother gets double (22.22) and the sister gets single (11.11). Footnote: (a) If there are more than two daughters, for them is two-thirds of the estate. And if there are male and female brothers, the male has double the female. (b) So if there are two or more full sisters, for them is two-thirds. And with them, there is no inheritance for consanguine sisters unless there is a consanguine brother with them. So if there is a consanguine brother, begin the division with those who have fixed shares, give them, then if there is a surplus, divide among the consanguine siblings, male double female. If nothing remains, nothing for them.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the book of inheritance (faraid) explaining the condition under which consanguine sisters (father's side sisters) are excluded by full sisters. The matn states that when full sisters (from both mother and father) take their two-thirds share, consanguine sisters (from father only) are excluded unless they have a consanguine brother who makes them asabah. The commentator expands: if there are two or more full sisters, they take two-thirds of the estate. Since there is no residue, consanguine sisters get nothing. However, if a consanguine brother is present, after giving full sisters their two-thirds, the remaining one-third goes to the consanguine brother as asabah, and the consanguine sisters inherit along with him in the ratio of 2:1 (male:female). The proof is from Quran 4:176 (the verse about kalalah) which assigns two-thirds to two or more sisters, and then addresses mixed siblings with the male double female rule. Additionally, a hadith from Bayhaqi is cited: when full sisters are two or more, they take two-thirds; consanguine sisters get nothing unless they have a consanguine brother, in which case the surplus after prescribed shares is divided among them in the 2:1 ratio. The author provides a numerical example: base 100, full sisters get 66.66, consanguine brother gets 22.22, consanguine sister gets 11.11. The footnotes clarify the principle: for daughters (not sisters) two-thirds applies, and the general rule of male double female for mixed siblings.

Key Terms
اخوات لاب وام (akhawāt li ab wa umm): Full sisters: sisters sharing the same mother and father as the deceased.
اخوات لاب (akhawāt li ab): Consanguine sisters: sisters sharing the same father but different mother from the deceased.
عصبہ (ʿaṣabah): Residuary heir: a male relative who takes the remainder of the estate after fixed shares are assigned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When there is only one full sister.

C) When there are no other heirs.
D) When the full sisters are less than two.

Key Takeaway
Full sisters take two-thirds; consanguine sisters are excluded unless a consanguine brother is present, in which case they share the residue with him in a 2:1 ratio.

Father and Grandfather Inheritance States
Tabular overview of father and grandfather inheritance states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three states of the father and four states of the grandfather in Hanafi inheritance, and identify the share in each condition.

Core Idea
Father's share depends on presence of children; grandfather is excluded by father.

This passage is a quick-reference table from the Siraji, a standard Hanafi inheritance manual. It first lists the twelve heirs who receive fixed shares (four males and eight females), then details the conditions under which the father and grandfather inherit. Understanding these states is essential for correctly calculating inheritance shares in real cases.

Guided Path
1
List the twelve fixed-share heirs
Memorize the twelve persons: father, grandfather, consanguine brother, husband (males); wife, full daughter, granddaughter, full sister, consanguine sister, uterine sister, mother, grandmother (females).
These are the primary sharers in Quranic inheritance.
2
Understand father's three states
The father inherits differently based on the presence of children or grandchildren. There are three scenarios: (1) one-sixth only when a son or agnatic grandson exists; (2) one-sixth plus residue when a daughter or agnatic granddaughter exists; (3) entire estate as asabah when no children or grandchildren exist.
The father is never totally excluded; his share varies.
3
Understand grandfather's four states
The grandfather's states mirror the father's but with a fourth: he is completely excluded if the father is alive. Otherwise: (1) one-sixth with son/grandson; (2) one-sixth plus residue with daughter/granddaughter; (3) all as asabah when no descendants.
The grandfather's exclusion (sāqit) is total when the father exists.
4
Note the key difference
The grandfather's fourth state (exclusion) is unique; the father never gets excluded. This distinction is crucial in inheritance calculations.
Remember: father always inherits; grandfather may be blocked.

و حصوں کی یہ ترتیب سراجی سے ماخوذ ہے، حصوں سے مراد سہام ہیں جو قرآن اور احادیث میں کسی حصے دار کو دیئے گئے ہیں۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part Four. Conditions of Heirs at a Glance. There are twelve persons who take shares: four males and eight females. Males who take shares: (1) father, (2) grandfather, (3) consanguine brother, (4) husband. Females who take shares: (1) wife, (2) full daughter (son's daughter), (3) granddaughter, (4) full sister, (5) consanguine sister, (6) uterine sister, (7) mother, (8) grandmother. Male shares: (1) Father has three states. As asabah. In which state which share will be given: When there is a son or son's son or son's son's son: (1) only one-sixth share. (2) one-sixth and as asabah. (3) only as asabah. [Values: X, 16.66, 16.66, X, 33.33 when there is daughter or granddaughter or great-granddaughter; 100 when there is no son, no grandson, no daughter, no granddaughter.] (2) Grandfather has four states. Shares as asabah. In which state which share: When there is a son or grandson or great-grandson: (1) only one-sixth. (2) one-sixth and as asabah. (3) only as asabah entirely. (4) grandfather will be excluded. [Values: X, 16.66, 16.66, X, 33.33 when there is daughter or granddaughter or great-granddaughter; 100 when no son, no grandson, no daughter, no granddaughter; X when father is present.] This arrangement of shares is taken from Siraji; 'shares' refer to the portions (siham) given in Quran and hadith to any share-holder.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents a quick reference table of the heirs who receive fixed shares in inheritance. It lists twelve persons: four males (father, grandfather, consanguine brother, husband) and eight females (wife, full daughter, granddaughter, full sister, consanguine sister, uterine sister, mother, grandmother). Then it details the conditions for the father and the grandfather. The father has three states: (1) if there is a son or agnatic grandson (son's son) even lower, the father receives only one-sixth as a fixed share; (2) if there is a daughter or agnatic granddaughter, the father gets one-sixth plus the residue as asabah; (3) if there are no children or grandchildren at all, the father takes everything as asabah. The grandfather also has four states: similar to the father, but additionally (4) the grandfather is completely excluded (sāqit) when the father is alive. The shares are given in numerical values: one-sixth is 16.66%, one-sixth plus residue (when daughter present) is 33.33% (one-sixth plus asabah residue), and 100% when sole heir. The source is Siraj al-Din al-Sajawandi's Siraji, a standard Hanafi manual on inheritance. The 'shares' (sihām) refer to the prescribed fractions from Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
باپ (bāp): Father of the deceased; a male heir who can take fixed share and/or residue.
دادا (dādā): Paternal grandfather of the deceased; an heir who takes similar to father but is excluded by father.
عصبہ (ʿaṣabah): Residuary heir; the male relative who takes the remainder after fixed shares are distributed.
صلبی بیٹی (ṣalbī bīṭī): Daughter of the deceased herself (not granddaughter).
پوتی (pūtī): Agnatic granddaughter: son's daughter of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What share does the father receive when the deceased leaves a son?
A) One-sixth as a fixed share.
B) One-sixth plus the residue as asabah.
C) The entire estate as asabah.
D) Nothing, he is excluded by the son.

Key Takeaway
Father's inheritance share depends on presence of children; grandfather is excluded by father.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
6 min
Father's Three States in Inheritance
Listing the three states of the father's inheritance share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of the father's inheritance share in Hanafi faraid and apply them to calculate his portion.

Core Idea
The father's share depends on the deceased's descendants: 1/6 if a male child exists, 1/6 + residue if a female child exists, and full residue if no child.

In Hanafi faraid, the father is a primary heir whose share varies based on the presence of descendants. This lesson unpacks the three distinct states outlined in the classical texts, enabling you to determine his exact portion in any given estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the father as an heir
The father is always an heir; his share is prescribed by the Quran. First, confirm he is present and not excluded by any other heir (he is never excluded in Hanafi law).
2
Check the presence of male descendants
If the deceased has a son, grandson, or great-grandson (male descendants), the father receives only the fixed one-sixth (1/6) share. No residue goes to him.
This applies even if there are multiple male descendants.
3
Check the presence of only female descendants
If the deceased has a daughter, granddaughter, or great-granddaughter (female descendants) but no male descendants, the father receives one-sixth (1/6) as a fixed share and also takes the remaining residue as an asabah (residuary heir).
The asabah share can be more than the 1/6, often 1/6 + remainder.
4
Determine the share when no descendants exist
If the deceased has no children or grandchildren (neither male nor female), the father inherits the entire estate as an asabah (residuary heir) after any other fixed shares (e.g., spouse's share).
In this case, he may receive 100% of the residue or the whole estate if there are no other heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باپ کی حالتیں : تین ہیں۔
بطور عصبہ
کس حالت میں کون سا حصہ ملے گا
(1) صرف چھٹا حصہ ملے گا X 16.66 جب بیٹا ہو یا پوتا ہو یا پر ہوتا ہو۔
(۲) چھٹا حصہ اور عصبہ کے طور پر X 16.66 X 33.33 جب بیٹی ہو یا پوتی ہو یا پر پوتی ہو۔
(۳) صرف عصبہ کے طور پر X 100 جب نہ بیٹا ہو نہ پوتا ہو نہ بیٹی ہونہ پوتی ہو۔
The states of the father: three. As asabah. In which state which share will be given: (1) Only one-sixth will be given – X 16.66 – when there is a son, or a grandson, or a great-grandson. (2) One-sixth and as asabah – X 16.66 X 33.33 – when there is a daughter, or a granddaughter, or a great-granddaughter. (3) Only as asabah – X 100 – when there is no son, no grandson, no daughter, no granddaughter.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the father's inheritance shares in Hanafi faraid. The passage outlines three distinct scenarios: First, if the deceased has a son or any male descendant (grandson, great-grandson), the father receives only a fixed one-sixth share. Second, if the deceased has a daughter or any female descendant (granddaughter, great-granddaughter), the father receives one-sixth as a fixed share and then additionally takes the residue as an asabah. Third, if there are no children or descendants at all, the father inherits the entire remaining estate as an asabah after any other fixed shares. The percentages (16.66 for 1/6, 33.33 likely for the asabah portion in the second case, and 100 for full residue) help visualize the shares. This is a standard summary from the Sirajiyyah.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): A residuary heir who takes whatever remains after the fixed shares are distributed.
چھٹا حصہ (chhata hissah): One-sixth share (1/6), a Quranic fixed share for the father in the presence of a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the father receive only one-sixth (1/6) as a fixed share?
A) When the deceased has a son or male descendant
B) When the deceased has a daughter only
C) When there are no children
D) When the deceased has a mother

Key Takeaway
The father's share in Hanafi faraid is determined by the presence of descendants: 1/6 with a male descendant, 1/6 plus residue with only female descendants, and full residue with no descendants.
